bad characteristics, mainly because every relationship has Linkages and Clashes (and
everyone has transits that influence whether the focus is on the linkages or the clashes).

USER'S GUIDE FOR MAGISOFT VERSION 2.36

THE MAIN SCREEN
When you first run MagiSoft v. 2.36, you will see the MAIN SCREEN. This Main
Screen will look very much like the diagram of the sample screen that is a few pages below. The
Main Screen of your MagiSoft program may vary from the sample depending on the exact
version and level of software that you have. But in all cases, the Main Screen is divided into the
following five sections:
1) The largest section is the GRAPHICS AREA and displays the Magi AstroChart; below the
Magi AstroChart are two sections; and to the right of the Magi AstroChart are the other two
sections.
2) The area below the Magi AstroChart and covering the leftmost third of the screen is the LEFT
DATA GRID. This is a scrollable window that contains astrological data. If you press <Page
Down> or <Page Up>, the data behind the window of this Scroll Area will scroll up or down.
3) The section immediately to the right of the Left Data Grid is the MIDDLE DATA GRID and
also displays astrological data. One Scroll Area contains the data for the longitudes and the other
261

Scroll Area contains the data for the declinations. The <Page Up> and <Page Down> keys do not
work on this Scroll Area; they only work in the Left Data Grid.
4) To the right of the Graphics Area and the Middle Data Grid, there are the final two sections.
The one on top is the DATA ENTRY AREA and it covers the upper half of the screen to the right
of the Graphics Area. There are at least 24 boxes in this area, and each box accepts data that you
can give to the program; for example, on the third line there is a box marked “Date.” This is the
DATE BOX and is where you want to enter the birth date that you want the program to use when
it draws the Magi AstroChart. The date in the Date Box is called the Chart Date. Some of the 24
boxes allow you to enter other data like the time of the Chart Date, and the name for the Chart
Date. The other boxes allow you to select to turn on or turn off certain functions of the program.
The purpose of all of the 24 boxes are explained in the section below entitled "The Data Area has
24 Boxes and.”
5) Beneath the Data Entry Area is the fifth section and we call it the DATA DISPLAY AREA,
the positions of all the planets for the Chart Date are displayed in this area. If you have a monitor
that is recently manufactured, this area will not be scrollable and the display will have all of the
astrological data for the Chart Date. But if you have an older monitor, this area will be scrollable,
and you will need to scroll down to see all of the data.
The Magi Society is constantly improving its software. Your MagiSoft v. 2.36 has menus for all
of the features that most members normally use. As you can see from your MagiSoft screen,
there are some menus listed along the Menu Bar (the horizontal bar just below the top bar that has
the MagiSoft title). Your MagiSoft v. 2.36 is an improvement over our original program,
versions 2.00 through 5.43. None of those prior programs had drop-down menus. Although your
new MagiSoft v. 2.36 does have several drop-down menus, there are just a few features of the
program that are not accessible through any of the available menus, and such features must
therefore be accessed through hotkeys (to be explained later). As is the case with most Windows
programs, most selections on the menus also have hotkeys that are alternative ways to access the
same features. In these instructions, from time to time, we will interchange from using menus to
hotkeys so you get used to the idea of using either one. This is standard with Windows programs
and if you are confused by what you just read, please just read on and you will understand what
we mean.
Now let us get started right away on using MagiSoft. We are going to give you a super

CREATING A BIRTH CHART
Load MagiSoft v. 2.36 by double-clicking on its icon (the one that looks like the earth).
Once the program is fully loaded, your computer screen will display what looks like the sample
screen of a MagiSoft program shown below:

Figure 124 main screen of magisoft

This screen layout is called the Main Screen. The Magi AstroChart that is in the large
rectangle on the left and middle part of your screen is the chart of the day and time that is given to
MagiSoft by your computer's internal clock. Now click the ENTER DATA button (located about
1 to 2 inches below the right upper corner of your screen. A blue background will appear in a
box near the upper right hand corner of your screen. That box is called the DATE BOX and is

263

the place where you can enter any birth date. Enter your birth date now by typing your birth date;
we will always use this format: mm/dd/yyyy.
Or if the month and day has only one digit, you can type in m/d/yyyy. But always use 4
digits for the year! Let’s use an example and start with the birth date of Bill Gates. He was born
October 28, 1955. Type in "10/28/1955" (when we use quote marks like this, type in only what is
inside the quotes marks; please do not type in the actual quote marks). If you make a mistake,
you can first use the <Backspace> key to erase the old data and then you can type in the new data.
Once you type in the correct date, press <Tab> and check the Date Box to make sure you entered
the correct information. When you press <Tab>, the blinking cursor should move to the Time
Box (which is the next box) and it should now be blue. To go back to the Date Box, simply hold
down the <Shift> key and at the same time, press the <Tab> key; the blinking cursor will move
backwards each time you do this and the blue background will move with the cursor.

CREATING YOUR CHART
Bill Gates' birth date is only an example; what we really want is to enter our own
birth date into the Date Box. Please do that using the methods we have just explained.
Hold down the <Ctrl> and press <D> and the Name Box will become blue
inside. Now enter your birth date using the format of mm/dd/yyyy. After you have
entered your birth date into the Date Box, press <tab>; the Time Box just to the right of
the Date Box will become blue inside. If you read the time in the Time Box, you will see
that the time in it will be the time that is on your computer and this matches the time
shown on the lower right corner of your computer's screen. But MagiSoft will express
this time in the format of military time, which means that it is a 24 hour clock, and not a
12 hour clock. Even though the chances are you were not born at noon, for now, we
want you to enter a time of noon into the Time Box. Type in "12.00" and press the <tab>
key. The number '12:00' should now be in the Time Box; this is probably not your birth
time but it is close enough for our purposes since we are only going to create a CAC and
check for interaspects of the planets.
We are not going to worry about your exact time of birth right now. We will
teach you about entering exact times later. In this super quick tour, we just want to get a
Magi AstroChart of your birthday up on the screen as quickly as possible. To do that,
now that your birth date has been entered into the Date Box, just click on the
RECALCULATE BUTTON (located about 3 inches below the upper right corner of your
screen). Presto, the chart that is displayed is now the Magi AstroChart of the day you
were born! It is as simple as that.
To make the Magi AstroChart full screen, hold down <ctrl> and press <G> at
the same time. The Magi AstroChart will now be the size of your whole computer
screen except that there is a large box on the right of your screen containing a lot of data.
We will explain how to read this data later. But you can get rid of this box by just
holding down <ctrl> and pressing the <A> key. Now let us go back to the Main Screen;
we do that by holding down <ctrl> and pressing the <G> key again.
(At this point we would like to emphasize that there is nothing to be afraid of
with MagiSoft. If you make mistakes and do not know how to undo the mistake, simply
shut down the program and reload it to start all over. You can close MagiSoft in the
same way you close any other Windows program, by clicking the File Menu and then
selecting the Exit choice. You can restart MagiSoft again by double-clicking its icon.)
Before we go on and create a CAC between you and a person you have an
interest in, we want to put your name on the Magi AstroChart. To do this, locate the
Name Box near the top of the screen just to the right of the large box that contains the

264

Magi AstroChart (please refer to the sample screen layout above). The Name Box is
marked with the word 'Name' just to the left of the actual box. Whenever you first load
MagiSoft, the Name Box will have the word 'Today' inside it. Point the mouse just to the
right of the word 'Today' and click the left mouse button. A blinking cursor should
appear inside the box just after the word 'Today'. Use the <Backspace> key to erase
'Today'; then type in your name, and press the <tab> key to make the MagiSoft
program accept the name you typed in. Now the program has stored your name, but it
does not yet display it on the chart. To display your name on the upper left corner of the
Magi AstroChart, click on the RECALCULATE button.

CREATING A CAC AND CHECKING FOR LINKAGES
The next step is to show you how easy it is to create a CAC (Combined
Alignment Chart) and check what linkages you form with any other person. If you
recall, in our book about love and money, we refer to this other person as the Connected
Person. To find out what linkages you have with any Connected Person, all you have to
do is to tell the MagiSoft program the birth date of the Connected Person. This is easy to
do. The first step is to click the CREATE CAC menu, which is located on the top of your
screen, and select BIRTHDATA FOR RED PLANETS. By doing this, you will open the
COMPARISON WINDOW which is a pop-up window that will look like the one below.

(On some computer systems, the bottom of this window may not be fully
viewable. If this is the case with your computer, you can move the window up to see
the bottom of the window. To move the window up, point the mouse to any spot on the
blue bar at the top of the Comparison Window, hold down your left mouse button and
move the mouse up an inch. This should move the window. Now let go of the mouse.)
The Comparison Window (the pop-up window) is labeled "Comparison DataBirth Data for red planets.” We will always refer to it as the Comparison Window.
There are seven boxes in this window and each one allows you to enter data about the
Connected Person. We will teach you about every one of these boxes later in these
instructions but right now, we just want to teach you how to enter the birth date and
name of the Connected Person. This is enough for you to find out the linkages and
activations that the two of you make.
The first and biggest box in the pop-up window has the word 'Name' outside
and to the left of the box. Please point your mouse to the Name Box of the Comparison
Window and click the left mouse button. A blinking vertical cursor should appear. We

265

want the cursor to be at the leftmost part of the Name Box so if you have to, use the
<Backspace> key to move the cursor to the leftmost part of the box and then type in the
name of the Connected Person, then press <Tab>. The box just below the Name Box
should now have the blinking cursor and will be blue; this is the box to enter the birth
date of the Connected Person. Type in the birth date of the Connected Person using this
format: mm/dd/yyyy, and then press <tab>. (As was the case earlier, you must enter
four digits for the year). The program will convert your data and display a date in the
Date Box and move you to the Time Box, which is the next box and this should now
have a blinking cursor in it and will be blue. (Check to make sure you entered the right
date. If you need to re-enter the birth date, use <Shift> + <Tab> to go back to the Date
Box. Once you know the date is correct, and you are in the Time Box, you need to enter
the time of birth of the Connected Person. Here again, for the purposes of this super
quick tour, we will use noon as the time of birth. Enter "12.00" and press the <Tab> key.
Then click the button marked 'Done' at the bottom of the window. By clicking the Done
Button, the MagiSoft program stores the birth date of the Connected Person, and closes
the Comparison Window. You have now stored the birth data of the Connected Person.
The next step to creating the CAC is to overlay the Connected Person's chart on
top of yours. As you know, a CAC is created by overlaying one person's birth chart on
top of another person's birth chart. Your MagiSoft program makes it easy to distinguish
which planets belong to which person by making one person's planets FLASH IN RED
while the other person's planets are black. But sometimes, you may not want every
planet to be included in the CAC. For example, you may want to look at a CAC that
only shows the other person's Jupiter and Chiron, or only the other person's Saturn.
MagiSoft has a fabulous feature that lets you select which planets you want to flash in
red. You can choose to have them all flash in red, or any combination you wish. To tell
the MagiSoft program which planets you want to flash in red, you use the Planets to
Overlay Window. To open this window, hold down <ctrl> and press <V> at the same
time. (In the future, for ease of writing, when we want you to press two keys down at
the same time, we will use the following format: "please enter [<ctrl> + <V>].") A popup window will appear and it will be labeled 'Planets to Overlay' just like the one below:

On the left half of this pop-up window, you will see a listing of all of the planets
plus the node, ascendant, midheaven and vertex. If you have the Asteroids Upgrade,
the window will also list the abreviations of the four major asteroids just as is the case in
the sample illustration above.
To demonstrate to you how this pop-up window works, please point the arrow
of the mouse at the abbreviation 'JUP', hold down the <Ctrl> key and at the same time
please click the left mouse button. When you do this, the abbreviation 'JUP' will turn

266

blue in the background; this tells MagiSoft to overlay the Connected Person's Jupiter on
top of your chart. Now click the OK button that is located in the Planets to Overlay
Window. When you do this, the pop-up window will disappear and the Connected
Person's Jupiter will be flashing in red on your chart on the computer's screen. There
will be a red Jupiter in the longitudes and another red Jupiter will be flashing in the
declinations. This demonstrates how the program works to create flashing red planets.
But now let us learn how to make all the planets from the Connected Person's
chart flash in red and overlay them on top of your planets. This is easy to do. To do
this, first reopen the Planets to Overlay Window. You can do this in one of two ways.
You can enter [<Ctrl> + <V>] and the Date Box will turn blue. (Alternatively, the other
way to open the Planets to Overlay Window is to click on the menu with the title "Create
CAC" and then click on Overlay Red Planets.) You will see the overlay window pop up
again and you should see that the background behind the abbreviation for Jupiter will
still be blue. If you click this abbreviation again (while holding down the <Ctrl> key),
the blue background will disappear, and it means the MagiSoft program will not overlay
Jupiter on your chart.

Whenever you make an abbreviation of a planet have a blue background, you are telling
the MagiSoft program to make that planet in the Connected Person's chart flash in red.
You can make the background blue for any planet that you want or for any combination
of planets that you want. Just make sure that you hold down the <Ctrl> key and click on
the abbreviation (or symbol) of the planet.
To get a feel of this feature, play with the listing of the planets and click them blue and click
them back to normal, all the time holding down the <Ctrl> key. Whenever a planet is
highlighted in blue, this tells MagiSoft to take the position of that planet in the chart of the
Connected Person, and overlay it over your chart. Let us overlay all of the planets by
clicking them all until they are each blue (but not the ASC (ascendant), MID (midheaven),
VTX (vertex) and NOD (True North Node). Once you have selected which planets you
want to overlay in a CAC, you must click the OK button that is located in the Planets to
Overlay Window. When you have done this, the pop-up window disappears and all of the
Connected Person's natal planets will be flashing in red on the computer screen while your
own planets are still displayed in black. In other words, MagiSoft now displays the
Combined Alignment Chart between you and the Connected Person. You can now see
how your chart matches up with that of the Connected Person, and try to pick out the
linkages and activations.
We now want to learn a shortcut as to how to make all of the Connected Person's planets
flash in red. Please reopen the Planets to Overlay Window but this time, instead of
clicking each planet one at a time, you can hold down the <Ctrl> key, point to the
abbreviation of the Sun, press the left mouse button and then at the same time slide the
mouse pointer down and touch each abbreviation of each planet. As you do this, each
abbreviation will become blue one at a time. When you finish making all the planets blue,
let go of the all of the keys and mouse. (This all works the same way as other Windows
based programs work.)
Now let us see how to draw lines connecting linkages and clashes in a CAC.

DRAWING LINES TO CONNECT LINKAGES OR CLASHES

267

A CAC with black and flashing red planets is not very helpful to us unless there are lines
connecting the linkages and clashes so that we can easily see them. Let us learn how to draw
these lines.
Our first step is to create a CAC that has all the Connected Person's planets flash in red.
We do this by opening the Planets to Overlay Window (enter [<Ctrl> + <V>]) and clicking on all
of the abbreviations of the planets (making sure to hold down the <Ctrl> key), and finally telling
the MagiSoft program to display the flashing red planets by clicking on the OK button in the
Planets to Overlay Window. You should now see a CAC with black planets and red planets.
To display lines connecting the linkages or clashes, please follow these two steps:
1. Click on the Create CAC menu, and select Calculate Interaspects/Transits
2. Click on the Select Line Angles Menu and select Clashes if you want to display lines
connecting the linkages (or select Linkages and Semi-linkages if you want to display lines
connecting the linkages and semi-linkages; a semi-linkage is a sextile)
The Select Line Angles Menu lets you choose other types of lines to connect. Play around
with them and click on each choice.

CALCULATING AND DISPLAYING LINKAGES AND ACTIVATIONS

different types of interaspects, such as linkages and activations. Once you have followed the

menu, and selecting CALCULATING INTERASPECTS/TRANSITS). Right after you do that,

SCREENING FOR LINKAGES ONLY, OR ACTIVATIONS ONLY
In any birth chart or CAC, there are quite a few aspects or interaspects. It you draw lines
between all of them, the resulting chart will have so many lines that it is usually quite difficult to
pick out the most important aspects or interaspects. Most often, what you really want to do is to
draw lines only for certain types of angles, like oppositions plus squares, or trines plus sextiles.
This is exactly what MagiSoft allows you to do.
MagiSoft Version 2.36 only draws the lines in black, but the more advanced versions
draws different line colors for certain sets of angles for your computer screen. You must have a
more advanced version of MagiSoft to have this advanced feature. Whenever you renew your
membership or order Upgrades you will have a more advanced version of MagiSoft.
If you click on the menu labeled "Select Line Angles,” you will get a drop-down menu
that gives you five choices; each choice is an Angle Type. If you click on any of the five Angle
Types, you will draw lines only for the angles that make up the Angle Type you selected. If you
choose Linkages and Semi-linkages, you will see lines drawn on the CAC. The MagiSoft
program will draw connecting lines in your Combined Alignment Chart for every interaspect that
is a 120-degree linkage, and also every interaspect that is 60 degrees. The 120-degree interaspect
(called trine) is a linkage and is very powerful. A 60-degree interaspect (called sextile) has the
influence of weak linkages so we call them SEMI-LINKAGES. The lines connect the actual
planets that create the linkage or semi-linkage. For example, if your Chiron is 120 degrees from
the Connected Person's Venus, there will be a line connecting your Chiron to the other person's
Venus.
To look for clashes (sometimes called activations), open the Select Line Angles menu
and click on Clashes. When you do that, all the clashes in your Combined Alignment Chart will
be connected with lines. Clashes are interaspects that are 90 or 180 degrees (respectively called
square and opposition).
To look for 150-degree linkages (called quincunx), select Quincunxes. To clear the CAC
of all lines, or to look at the declinations without being distracted by the lines in the longitudes,
enter [<Alt> + <O>] (the letter ‘O’ and not the number ‘0’); this clears lines.
There are two other selections in the Select Line Angles menu: Quintiles and BiQuintiles, and All 30 Degree Angles. They are self-explanatory; click on them and see what you
get. Whenever you click on any of the five Angle Types in the Select Line Angles Menu, you
should notice that the lines on the CAC change and also the data in the Left Data Grid changes.
This is because that Grid lists the interaspects in the longitudes, and whenever you click on any of
the five Angle Types, it tells the program to only list the type of interaspects that match the Angle
Type you selected. For example, when you select Clashes, only the 90-degree and 180-degree
activations are listed in the Left Data Grid, and only those clashes are displayed with connecting
lines on the CAC (Combined Alignment Chart).
Next we need to look at the MagiSoft listings of interaspects and learn how to read them.
The info is most easily viewable if you go to Full Screen Graphics Mode by entering [<Ctrl> +

269

<G>]. When you do that, the CAC will be the size of your computer's screen and there is a
rectangular window on the right side with data in it. This data is a listing of interapects that you
form with the Connected Person. The types of interaspects that are listed depend on which of the
five Angle Types you selected from the Select Line Angles menu.
Unfortunately, in Full Screen Mode, there are no menus. But you can still instruct
MagiSoft which Angle Type you select.
If you enter <F10>, the listing of interaspects will include linkages of 120-degrees and
60-degrees, which are the ones that the <F10> function draws lines for. But this listing will also
include another form of linkage that the program does not draw lines for. When you enter <F10>,
the listing will include the 0-degree interaspects (called conjunctions) and these are included
because they are linkages, just like the 120-degree interaspects. But they do not have lines
connected the planets that form a conjunction because there is not enough space between the two
planets to draw a noticeable line.
When you enter <F9>, the listing gives you only the 150-degree type linkages; <F11>
gives you both the 90-degree and the 180-degree activations. By entering <F12>, you get all
quintiles and bi-quintiles. And if you enter <F5>, you get lines connecting all 30-degree type
angles (any angle that is a multiple of 30 degrees).

TURNING OFF THE RED FLASHING PLANETS TEMPORARILY
Quite often, it is useful to just turn off the red flashing planets to look at a less cluttered
chart.
You can turn off the red flashing planets by entering [<Alt> + <V>] at any time. To get the red
flashing planets back, re-enter [<Alt> + <V>]. Now Please make sure the red flashing planets are
on when you continue with these instructions.
The next step is to learn how to read the listings of interaspects.

HOW TO READ THE LISTINGS OF INTERASPECTS
When you installed the upgrade to MagiSoft v. 2.36, the installation included three
sample birth charts. We will now read one of them to help explain how to read the listings of
interaspects, and other astrological data that MagiSoft provides.
Click the File Menu and then click on Load. This will open the standard Windows Load
pop-up window. The blue bar at the top of this pop-up window will say something to the effect
“Select file to load options from…” Please navigate to the \MagiSoft directory and click it open.
Now the largest box in this pop-up window will list three files named “billpaul.opt, clinton.opt
and jones.opt.” (Not necessarily in that order.) Point the arrow of the mouse to the filename
“billpaul.opt” and click once; the background of that filename will turn blue. Now double-click
on that filename. The pop-up window will disappear and a new chart will be on the screen in the
Graphics Area.
In the upper left corner of your computer screen, it will say “Bill Clinton” and in the
upper right corner it will say “Comparison: Paula Jones.” Please enter [<Alt> + <8>] to calculate
interaspects. Now please enter <F1>. The bottom left two-thirds of your computer screen should
contain two grids with the following data. (Do not be concerned if there is less data because the
amount of data depends on the size and quality of your computer screen. You should also not be
concerned if some lines of data are missing because that will be explained later in these
instructions. This diagram is the same one we showed you a couple of pages ago.

270

(GRID DIAGRAM TWO)

Figure 126 grid-diagram in magisoft

There are two distinct grids above. One is called the Left Data Grid and the other is the
Middle Data Grid.
In the Left Data Grid, there is a listing of the interaspects that Bill Clinton and Paula
Jones have. The information about each interaspect is listed horizontally, one at a time. Please
note that each horizontal row has seven columns. The first column simply lists the number of
interaspects, so the first column vertically will always read 1, 2, 3, 4, etc.
The second and fourth columns give you the symbols of the planets that form the
interaspect, and the third column gives you the angle of the interaspect, such as 060, 120, and
000. With Clinton and Paula, the first interaspect is translated to be “Saturn 150 degrees from
Sun, with an orb of 0.41 degrees.” The astrological glyph for the symbol of the Connected
Person's natal planet is listed in the second column and the symbol for the Chart Person’s natal
planet that creates the linkage is in the fourth column. In this case Paula is the Connected Person
and Bill Clinton is the Chart Person (the person whose birth data appears in the Date Box of the
Main Screen).
The fifth column simply gives you the orb of the interaspect as measured in degrees with
either the letter 's' or the letter 'a' in front of the number. If the fifth column says 'a0.41', it means
the orb of the interaspect is 0.41 (meaning the two planets making the interaspect are 0.41 degrees
apart). The letters 'a' and 's' respectively mean ‘applying’ or 'separating' and such distinctions can
sometimes be important when you analyze interaspects.
The sixth column provides the time orb (labeled ‘Exact’) and the seventh column gives us
the time to exactness (labeled ‘Exact-Time’) and is not important for interaspects, so we advise
that you simply ignore them when it comes to compatibility analysis. The reason we give them to
you is that if you want to become a serious astrologer, they are crucial in other areas of astrology
like transits, which we will explain later.
Continuing with the listing of the interaspects, the second interaspect says that Paula’s
Chiron is 150 degrees from Clinton’s Sun and this interaspect has an orb of 2.12 degrees. The
third interaspect is Sun 30 Sun, which means the two persons’ Suns make an interaspect with an
angle of 30 degrees.
Note that the last viewable interaspect is numbered 6, but there are many more that you
cannot view behind the window. To see the others, you can click on the appropriate Scroll
Button, or you can enter the <Page Dn> key. Each time you enter <Page Dn>, you see more
interaspects. Some of the interaspects are at an angle of 72 or 144 degrees, which we did not
discuss in any of our books. We include them because we will probably talk about them in a
future book; they are very complicated to interpret and we suggest you ignore them for now. The
same is true for interaspects that are 45 degrees, and 135 degrees, etc.
If you want to be able to view more interaspects at one time, enter [<Ctrl> + <G>]. This
will take you to the Full Screen Mode and you will see many more interaspects. Sometimes, you

271

will still have to use the <Page Dn> to view more of them. But if you are interested in only
linkages, just enter <F10> and all the linkages will be listed and they almost always fit on one
page of the screen.
If you enter <F11>, you get all the clashes (activations).
What we still need to learn is how to get a listing of the interaspects in the declinations.
Please go back to the Main Screen by entering [<Ctrl> + <G>]. Note that the interaspects in the
longitudes are in the Left Data Grid and the data is scrollable. The interaspects in the declinations
are in the Middle Data Grid. When we want to see more of what is in the Left Data Grid, we can
press <Page Dn> or <Page Up>. These two keys can only work on one scroll area at a time so
they do not work on the Middle Scroll Area. But there is a way to instruct the MagiSoft program
to switch the declinations data (now in the Middle Data Grid) with the data for the longitudes
(now in the Left Data Grid) so that we can scroll the listing of the declinational interaspects; to do
this enter [<Alt> + <9>]. The two listings will now be reversed and the interaspects in the
declinations will now be in the Left Data Grid and will now be scrollable. Enter <Page Dn> to
see what we mean. More importantly, if you now go to the Full Graphics Mode by entering
[<Ctrl> + <G>], the interaspects in the declinations will be listed in the area that the longitudinal
interaspects were listed before. You see, the difference between [<Alt> + <8>] and [<Alt> +
<9>] is that the 8 lists the longitudinal interaspects in the Left Data Grid and the 9 lists the
declinational interaspects in the Left Data Grid. Whenever you use [<Ctrl> + <G>] to go to the
Full Graphics Screen, you will see a listing of whatever is in the Left Data Grid.
Now let us enter <F9>; this tells the MagiSoft program to draw in the lines for all
interaspects that have the 150 degree angle. If you have not deviated from these instructions, you
will see that the program has drawn in five lines. One of them connects the flashing red Saturn to
the black Sun in Leo. The red Saturn belongs to Paula and the black Sun is Clinton’s natal Sun.
(From time to time, you may want to remove the lines that are drawn to connect the
planets that form the interaspects. To do this, enter [<Alt> + <0>].
If you enter <F12>, the program will give you the 72-degree and 144-degree interaspects,
but we did not deal with them in any of our books yet. We suggest that for now, you ignore them.
But we have built them into your program because we will discuss them in a future book. The
results of interaspects that are 72 or 144 degrees are very complicated and require almost a whole
new book to understand.
Finally, if you enter <F1>, you will obtain a complete listing of interaspects of all angles.
This means that with <F1>, the listing of interaspects will include every 30 degree type of
interaspect, the 72 and 144-degree interaspects, the 45 and 135-degrees ones, etc. With all these
aspects, when you enter <F1>, there are no connecting lines because there would be too many of
them.
(If you do something to the program you are not supposed to, you might not get any
connecting lines if you enter <F9> through <F12>. If this happens, there is no need to panic.
The program will readjust; all you have to do is enter <F1>, and then use any of the <F9> through
<F12> keys, and the program will give you the appropriate lines again.)

TRANSITS
In our Love and Money book, we talked about a concept called natalization.
Natalization is the name we gave to the theory that when anything happens for the first time, that
thing is born and has a birth chart; the key is that the astrological energy of the moment of time of
birth is retained. Of course this is especially true about the birth of a person. The astrological
energy of the moment a person is born is retained by that person for a lifetime. We think that this

272

is why interaspects work. The astrological energies of two persons are interacting in their
relationship and the results are predictable.
Now let us take this a step further. Every day, as the planets move in the sky and create
new alignments, the planets in the sky also are signs of the astrological energy of the moment.
When a planet creates a transit, the transit creates a result very similar to the energy of the same
interaspect that occurs with a person. In other words, when a person was born with Jupiter in say
12 degrees of Aries, and that person’s Jupiter forms a Jupiter-Chiron Golden Linkage with a
Connected Person, then the results of the Golden Linkage are very similar to the results of a
transit that would occur whenever Jupiter is in 12 degrees of Aries.
In other words, there is remarkable similarity between a transit and an interaspect. For
this reason, MagiSoft is designed so that transits are treated in the same way that interaspects are.
With the MagiSoft program, you can calculate transits by using the Comparison Button. An
example will explain exactly how to do this.
Please load the file ‘clinton.opt’. You do this by clicking on the File Menu, then click on
‘Load’, and load ‘clinton.opt’ by double-clicking on that listing in the largest box of the pop-up
window that opens when you clicked ‘Load’. Clinton’s birth chart should appear on the screen.
Now open the Comparison Window by clicking the Comparison Button. You should find that the
date ‘05/09/1999’ is in the Date Box of the Comparison Window. As is the case with the Date
Box of the Main Screen, MagiSoft uses the U.S. convention of dates, which is MM/DD/YYYY.
Let us find out what Clinton’s transits were on the day he won the 1996 presidential elections. To
do this, click the Date Box of the Comparison Window. There should now be a cursor at the end
of the date and the data will have a blue background. Please enter ‘11/5/1996’ (election day of
1996). Now change the name in the Name Box of the Comparison Window from ‘Today’ to
‘Election Day 1996’. Finally, click the Done Button at the bottom of the Comparison Window.
Now enter [<Alt> + <8>] to calculate transits (this is the same way we calculate interaspects
because they are really the same thing). Enter <F10>.
Assuming you left the red flashing planets on, you will now see that there is a red
flashing Chiron that is almost exactly on Clinton’s natal Jupiter, the black Jupiter in 23.2 degrees
of Libra. This is a remarkably powerful transit. In fact, our website explains that this is a
Cinderella Transit and a Golden Transit. If you enter <Page Dn> once, you should see that the
seventh transit listed is ‘Chiron 000 Jupiter’ and the sixth column of the listing tells us that the
transit was exact ‘-003.0d’, meaning the transit peaked 3.0 days ago. The exact date and time of
the peak of the transit is listed in the last column. This was a Golden Transit and helps to account
for the fact Clinton peaked in the polls three days before the election.

CHECKING FOR SYMMETRICAL COMBINED PLANETARY
GEOMETRY
One of the most important astrological influences on compatibility is the existence of
certain types of Combined Planetary Geometry in a CAC. When there is a Grand Trine in a
CAC, it means the two persons that form the CAC are extraordinarily compatible. And if the
Grand Trine is composed of planets that include Chiron and or Saturn, then a very long-term
relationship between the two persons is likely (the Chiron creates romantic attachment, whereas
the Saturn creates controlling bonds). It is easy to check for Grand Trines in CACs by using the
<F10> key. When you enter this key, you are telling MagiSoft to draw connecting lines between
every pair of planets that form 120-degree linkages. Grand Trines are composed of 120-degree
linkages. But sometimes, one side of a Grand Trine is formed by an aspect (that is 120 degrees)
as opposed to a linkage. For example, if you look at the chart of Clinton’s transits on 11/5/1996,

273

you will see that there actually is a Grand Trine between Clinton’s natal Saturn (at 2.1 degrees of
Leo) and transiting Saturn and transiting Pluto. Yet you might miss seeing this because the
transiting Pluto and Saturn are not connected by any line.
To solve this problem, we built in a special feature Please click on the
Commands/Interpret Menu and then click on the choice labeled "Swap charts in CAC"; this
switches the two dates. Note that now; the Clinton birth date is in the upper right hand corner,
whereas it used to be in the upper left hand corner, of the Graphics Area. This also switches
around the charts so that Clinton’s natal planets are in flashing red, while the planetary positions
of 11/5/1996 are in black. But there still is no Grand Trine drawn in because the transiting aspect
of Saturn-Pluto trine is still not connected with a line. To connect the line, enter [<Alt> + <F>].
This last instruction tells the MagiSoft program to connect all aspects for the 11/5/1996 chart as
well as the interaspects between the two charts; the actual aspects that are connected depends on
whether we last entered <F10>, <F9> or <F11>. If you now enter these different keys, you will
see the difference.
Searching for Symmetrical Combined Planetary Geometry is the hardest thing you have
to do in this program. If you are having problems getting the hang of it all, we suggest that you
call your most computer literate friend, and ask for help.
HOW TO SCROLL THE SCROLL AREAS
Whenever there is a scroll area, you can move (scroll) the data that is displayed up and
down, and also sideways. This is done using standard Windows operating system procedures.
Note that at most of the corners of the scroll areas, there is a little box with an arrowhead in the
middle of the box; we will refer to such boxes as SCROLL BUTTONS. When you move the
mouse, you will move a white arrow. If you point the white arrow to any of the Scroll Buttons,
and click the left mouse button, the data in the scroll area will move in the direction that the
arrowhead points to. From now on, whenever we say point the white arrow to “a certain area”
and click, what we mean is to move the mouse so that the white arrow is pointing right at “a
certain area” and click the left mouse button.
There is also something called a Scroll Box. This is the box that is the same size as a
Scroll Button, but has no arrowhead or anything in it, and is located between the Scroll Buttons.
If you point the white arrow to the Scroll Box that is at the bottom edge of the Left Data Grid, and
you hold down the left mouse button and move the mouse to the right or left, the data in the scroll
area will move in the direction of your mouse. This is known as “click and drag.”
WE PREFER TO USE DECIMALS
The Magi Society prefers to use decimals as opposed to degrees and minutes. The
MagiSoft program's graphics will always display the positions of the planets in degrees and
decimals; the Magi AstroChart does not ever display the positions of the planets in degrees plus
minutes. We believe this is much more user friendly and will help to bring more popularity to
astrology. The public has great trouble dealing with degrees and minutes.
However, in the Data Display area, those of you who are astrology purists can choose to
display the astrological data in decimal form, or you can tell MagiSoft to use degrees and
minutes. Simply point your mouse on the box labeled "Dgrs" (about an inch below the Date Box
of the Main Screen) and click the left mouse button to put a check mark in that box. Now all data
anywhere in the MagiSoft program (except for the Magi AstroChart) will be in degrees plus
minutes.

274

THERE ARE TWELVE MODES
The Magi Society’s computer software program has an astounding level of flexibility and
capabilities. MagiSoft v. 2.36 allows you to select any one of twelve modes and each mode is
selectable by using the Data Modes menu.
Each time you select a different mode, your MagiSoft program calculates a different set
of data. When you change modes, the data that is calculated will be displayed in the Left and
Middle Data Grids so this data will change whenever you change modes. Each mode is designed
to provide you with the type of astrological information that you want and need in order to make
the most accurate analysis.
You use the Data Modes menu to tell MagiSoft what type of data you want it to calculate.
Below are the specifics of the twelve different modes. They are not meant to be memorized; they
are listed for reference. We will explain each of them later in this User's Guide.
Mode 0: lists planetary positions in the Left Data Grid; both the longitudes and declinations are listed; the
Middle Data Grid will be blank;
Mode 1: lists interplanetary aspects in the longitudes in the Left Data Grid, and interplanetary aspects in the
declinations in the Middle Data Grid;
Mode 2: lists the same interplanetary aspects as mode 1 but reverses the areas in which they are displayed;
the Left Data Grid will have the declinations and the Middle Data Grid will have the longitudes; the reason
you may use this is that the <page up> and <page down> keys only work in the Left Data Grid;
Mode 3: lists all the midpoints in the Left Data Grid and the Middle Data Grid is blank;
Mode 4: lists longitudinal Magi Quads in the Left Data Grid, and declinational Magi Quads in the Middle
Data Grid;
Mode 5: lists MQs, as in mode 4, but in reverse Scroll Areas;
Mode 6: lists longitudinal Midpoint Crossings in the Left Data Grid and declinational ones in the Middle
Data Grid;
Mode 7: lists Midpoint Crossings, as in mode 6, but in reverse Scroll Areas;
Mode 8: is used to calculate interaspects and transits; with the longitudes in the Left Data Grid and the
declinations in the Middle Data Grid;
Mode 9: is also used to calculate transits/interaspects, but displays them in reverse in the Scroll Areas.

Mode 10: is also used to calculate transits and interaspects by midpoints, with the longitudes in
the Left Data Grid and the declinations in the Middle Data Grid. TO GO TO THIS MODE,
ENTER [<Alt> + <A>}
Mode 11: same as mode 10 but reverses the order in which the midpoint transits are displayed.
TO GO TO THIS MODE, ENTER [<Alt> + <B>].
<Page Down> and <Page Up> allows you to scroll data listed in the Left Data Grid.

275

THE DATA ENTRY AREA HAS 24 BOXES AND THREE BUTTONS
The data entry area has 24 distinct boxes in which you can enter data or turn on/off
switches. In addtion, there are three buttons, named "ENTER DATA,” “RECALCULATE” and
“COMPARISON.”
The Data Entry area is where you enter the birth date, time, and coordinates for the chart
you want the program to create. It is also this area that allows you to select the many options and
functions of your program. Below is a list of the specifics of all these 24 selection boxes. Your
MagiSoftware has enormous flexibility and allows you to customize how you want your program
to make its calculations. You can change the orb of aspects, and include or exclude certain
astrological parameters like the Moon, ascendant and midheaven. Note that there is a rectangular
button at the end of the eighth line labeled “Recalculate”. When you change the data in any of
the 24 boxes, the program will usually not recalculate data based on your new entries until you
enter <Tab> to tell the program to accept the data you entered, and then you must click the
“Recalculate” button. When you do click the “Recalculate” button, the program will recalculate
all the data based on the information and options in the 24 boxes.
For the first eight data entry boxes (all of which are located on the first three lines), after
you enter data in a box, you may move to the next box by hitting the <tab> key on your keyboard;
to go back one box, use <shift> + <tab>. Except that when you are in the second box (called the
DT box and had the "dt" label just to its left), you must enter <Tab> three times before the cursor
gets to the Place Box and makes that box blue. (This is because there are two very small buttons
just to the right of the DT box and these boxes are marked "-" and "+". We will explain their use
later.)
You can activate any box by moving your mouse arrow to point to the box and click the
left mouse button. This instructs the program that you want to change the data in that box. You
may do this to any boxes in any sequence you choose. When you point and click a box,
something will change in the box. Depending on which of the 24 boxes you are activating, there
are two possible changes that will occur:
a) If the box turns to a blue background, you can use the <backspace> to erase all the data all at
once and enter new data.
b) The other possibility when you click a box is a “check mark” will either disappear or appear,
depending on if there was a “check mark” before; by clicking such boxes, you are turning on /off
a function or option.
All of the 24 data fields, functions, and options are changeable by altering what is in the
24 boxes. We will explain below what each box is for one at a time; the boxes are referred to by
the words on the screen next to the box. For example, the first box on line four has the word
“Mode” just to the left of the box; for this reason, we call this box the Mode Box. Do not get
bogged down in these descriptions; they are provided for your reference and will be explained
again during the Quick Tour.
Name: This box lets you enter a name for the chart; usually you would want to enter the name of the person
for whom the chart is cast; you may type in any alphanumeric data you like and whatever you type in this
box will be displayed on the upper left of the Graphics Section, when you recalculate. Point your mouse's
arrow to this box, click it and try entering new data in this box and become familiar with it. When you
have entered what you want, press the <tab> key and click the Recalculate button; the name you entered
should be displayed on the first line in the upper left corner of the Graphics Section.

276

dt: dt. is the abbreviation for Delta. Note that just to the right of this box there are two small buttons
marked "-" and "+". The number inside the DT box when you load the MagiSoft program is 1.0d. This
number represents the INCREMENT, which means if you click the "+" button, the increment of the date in
the Date Box (line 3) is 1.0 days; if you click the "-" button, you will reduce the date in the Date Box by 1.0
days. This feature is great to allow you to visually see the movement of the planets day to day. You can
enter any number of days, hours, or minutes and also decimal amounts. Try it out! Point the mouse at the
"+" button and click the left mouse button and look at the date in the Date Box change; all the data on the
screen also changes and the planets will move appropriately.
Place: This box is for you to enter the place of birth; the program does not use this box for calculations but
only displays whatever is in this box underneath the name in the upper left corner of the Graphics Area.
Point the mouse arrow to this box and click. A vertical blinking line will appear where you pointed the
arrow. When you turn on the program, this box reads "New York City" but you can change it using the
same rules as a word processing program. Try it. Click on the box and then use the <Backspace> and
<Delete> keys to erase "New York City" and type in new data; press <Tab> to tell the program to accept
the new data. To actually display the name of the city you typed in, you need to click the Recalculate
Button.
Lat: This box is to enter the geographic latitude of the chart you want to create; point the mouse to this box
and click; it will turn blue; enter your new data. Changing this data is only needed if you want the program
to calculate the ascendant and midheaven, or Vertex. Otherwise you do not need to enter any data in this
box. The format is nnNnn or nnSnn.
Long: Same as the Lat box but is to be used to enter the geographic longitude of the chart.
tz: In this box you enter the time zone; the zone can be 0 to 12 and -1 to -12. You can also enter the unusual
time zones that use the half-hour, but you must type in the colon. For example, time zone HST is entered
as 10:30.
Mode: This box will display the mode you are in; there are twelve modes as listed earlier in this manual. It
is easiest to change modes if you use the Data Modes menu. But you can also use your mouse arrow to
point to this box, click, and then change the number in this box; then if you click the Recalculate Button,
the new mode will be in effect.
Degrees: The box for this is to the left of the word "Dgrs"; it allows you to select if you want your data in
degrees plus decimals or degrees plus minutes. The box begins empty and if you point the mouse to it and
click, there will be a check mark. If you click it again the check mark will disappear and the box will be
empty again. Each time you click, the data in the Data Display Section will change back and forth from
decimals to degrees plus minutes, or visa versa.
Auto/A: This is a very powerful and useful feature that no other software program has. This box allows
you to search and seek for the presence of a specific planet in aspects and will be dealt with fully later in
the section entitled "Auto search and Highlighting".
B: Same as Auto/A but controls a second planet as variable.
AppOnly: If you click on this box and get a check mark in it, then the program will list only applying
aspects in the Scroll Areas, and will not list any aspects that are separating.
All Comb: If you turn on this feature by clicking and getting a check mark in this box, you will get all
possible aspect listings in the Scroll Areas. This means that you will get a separate listing for the Jup/Plu
midpoint as well as the Plu/Jup midpoint even though they are really the same midpoint. In this way, each
midpoint is listed twice and the listing of midpoints is grouped by planets. This makes all midpoints easier
to find. Try this out, click this box and then enter [<Alt> +<3>] which will give you midpoints in the Left
Data Grid; use <Page down> and <Page Up> to scroll this data and click the AllComb button back and

277

forth to see the difference. When this box has a check mark in it, you get twice as many aspects because
they are listed twice so you can find them more easily.
AppSep: By turning on this feature, you are instructing the MagiSoft program to draw different types of
lines for applying aspects, as opposed to separating ones. The applying aspects have solid lines, and the
separating ones have dashes.
Orb: Lets you choose the orb of aspects in the longitudes that you want listed in the Scroll Areas; you can
enter decimals and the range is 0-9
Orb/d: This orb is for declinations and the range is 0-3 degrees
NN: The program starts with a check in this box; click it to exclude display and use of True North Node in
calculations of aspects and Magi AstroChart; the check tells the program to include it in all calculations and
displays. No other astrology program gives you the declination of NN.
ACMC: MagiSoft starts with a blank in this box; click this box with a check mark if you want to include
the use and display of the Ascendant and Midheaven in all calculations and graphics.
VT: This box, when checked, tells the program to include the Vertex in all calculations and graphics.
CH: Click this box and the program will include Chiron in every single chart and calculation.
Moon: This box, when checked, tells the program to include the Moon in all calculations and graphics.
15*offset: This box is to the left of the "15*offset" and is used for calculations that some members of the
Board of Governors of the Magi Society like to use but the calculations are not important and the function
is disabled in your MagiSoft 2.36 program; the box was not removed in case we want to enable the
calculation at a later date.
Exact: This box is located to the left of the "Exact" and gives you the option of turning on or turning off the
option of calculating the actual time when an aspect is exact, or was exact. We will explain this more in the
section entitled "The Exact Feature."
The boxes that allow only a check mark are called CHECK BOXES; as distinguished from the boxes that
accept data, which are called DATA BOXES. Depending on the upgrades that you have ordered, there are
11 to 15 Check Boxes and 13 Data Boxes.

THE RECALCULATE AND COMPARISON BUTTONS
The RECALCULATE button when clicked recalculates all aspects and the Magi
AstroChart based on the information and options that are in the above 24 or more boxes.
The COMPARISON button when clicked will open the Comparison Window, which
allows you to enter the birth data about a Connected Person or for the day of a transit. The use of
this button is covered under the section entitled “Calculating Transits and Displaying Red
Flashing Planets.” The Comparison Window can also be opened by clicking the Create CAC
menu and selecting Birth Data for Red Planets.

278

HOT KEYS
There are a few hot keys for your convenience. Below is a listing of the ones you will need to use.
[<Ctrl> + <D>]: This is a shortcut to the Date Box. Use this hot key combination to go right to the Date
Box so you can enter the birth date of the person for whom you wish to cast a chart.
[<Ctrl> + <G>]: This gives you the Full Screen Graphics mode; after you are in Full Screen Graphics, if
you re-enter this hot key combination, it will bring you back to the Main Screen. When hot keys change a
screen back and forth from one view to another, we use the term TOGGLE. The [<Ctrl> + <G>] toggles
the Full Screen Graphics with the Main Screen.
[<Ctrl> + <A>]: When you are in Full Screen mode, a large data window will appear on the right side of
the screen and the window will contain all the data from the Left Data Grid, but the window is much bigger
and will cover part of the Magi AstroChart. You can hide the large data window by entering [<Ctrl> +
<A>]. If you enter [<Ctrl> + <A>] a second time, the window reappears. This hot key toggles the large
data window on and off.
[<Ctrl> + <C>]: This tells the program to recalculate all data based on the information you gave it and
redraw the Magi AstroChart according to the data that is in the data boxes. IF YOU USE THIS HOTKEY,
YOU MUST ENTER <TAB> BEFORE YOU USE IT OR THE DATA WILL NOT BE ACCEPTED FOR
CALCULATION. It is actually much easier and better to just click the Recalculate Button, which works
even if you do not press <Tab>. (The MagiSoft program has this hotkey because our original software
versions have it but did not have the Recalculate Button and we want our original users to be able to use all
the old hotkeys in this program.)
[<Ctrl> + <N>]: This is a shortcut to getting today's Magi AstroChart up on the screen quickly. The
program will use your computer's internal clock and calculate all data based on its date and time; this
includes the Magi AstroChart.

[<Ctrl> + <V>]: Opens the Overlay Window, and allows you to select the planets you want to
overlay and flash in red.
[<Ctrl> + <X>]: Switches the birth data around so that the Chart Date becomes the Comparison
Date and the Comparison Date becomes the Chart Date; all the other birth data associated with
the Chart Date and Comparison Date are also switched.
[<Ctrl> + <O>]: Opens the Time Orb Filter that allows you to set MagiSoft to exclude all
aspects above a specified time orb parameter.
[<Alt> + <F>}: Usable only in modes 8 and 9; draws aspect lines connecting planets of the Chart
Date so that you can more easily see Symmetrical Combined Planetary Geometry.
[<Alt> + <Q>}: Aspects are normally listed by Magi Sequences or by planets; using this hotkey
combination sorts aspects and transits by time to exactness; press the hotkeys again and the
aspects are again listed by Magi Sequences or planets.
[<Alt> + <V>}: Removes all flashing red planets when the Overlay is activated; using this
hotkey comibination again tells MagiSoft to overlay red flashing planets again.
[<Ctrl> + <M>]: Opens the House Window to allow you to select House mode and choose
which of ten house systems you wish to use.

FUNCTION KEYS and FILTERS
There are also some function keys that are programmed to act as FILTERS to allow you
to choose the types of aspect lines you want to draw, and also to help you detect and analyze
special types of Planetary Geometry. When you are in modes 1 or 8 (and ONLY in these modes),
and you enter any of the following function keys, you will draw only certain types of lines:
F9:

draws all quincunxes
