DETAILS ABOUT MAGISOFT V.2.36
From our experience with other versions of our software programs, we learned that the
easiest way to help you learn MagiSoftware is to create a quick tour so that you can experience
the full capabilities of MagiSoftware by following step by step procedures. Hopefully, you
followed the instructions of the previous pages. It is now time to go into some more details of the
program. Again, we will help you learn them in the form of a quick tour. So please follow the
instructions on the rest of these pages as precisely as you can.
THE VERY BEGINNING
To begin running the program, double click on the MagiSoft icon. You should now see a
screen that looks something like the sample screen shown earlier in this manual. Your own
screen may be different depending on the level of software that you bought. The screen is
interactive with you in that you can change data on the screen to request the MagiSoftware
program to provide you with the astrological data that you are looking for. For example, you can
change the date, time, geographic coordinates, and time zone, and then instruct MagiSoftware to
calculate all astrological data and the chart based on your input.
If you want MagiSoft to cast a chart, begin by clicking the ENTER DATA button; the
Date Box will become blue. Now press the <Backspace> key; this erases the data that was in the
Date Box and you should see a blinking cursor in the Date Box with the box empty. You can
now simply type in the birth date you want the program to create a chart of. Type in the birthdate
but always use this format:
mm/dd/yyyy
Or if the month and day has only one digit, you can type in m/d/yyyy. ALWAYS
ENTER FOUR DIGITS FOR THE YEAR! Let’s use an example and start with the birth date of
Bill Gates. He was born October 28, 1955. Type in 10/28/1955. If you make a mistake, you can
first use the <Backspace> key to erase the old data and then you can type in the correct data.
Once you type in the correct data, press <Tab> and check to make sure you entered the correct
information. When you press <Tab>, the blinking cursor should move to the Time Box. To go
back to the Date Box, simply hold down the <Shift> key and at the same time, press the <Tab>
key; the blinking cursor will move backwards each time you do this.
Making sure that you are in the Time Box, let us enter a time of day in this box. First you
need to press the <Backspace> key to erase what was in it. Let us assume Bill Gates was born at
3 PM. The Time Box accepts data ONLY IN MILITARY TIME FORMAT. In other words, 3
PM is 15:00 and 3 AM is 3:00. Enter 15 and press <Tab>. The 00 is not necessary. But if you
enter minutes, make sure you place a colon or a decimal point between the hour and the minutes.
If you want to enter 3:28 PM, you can type in 15.28 or 15:28.
Once you have entered the birth time, please press <Tab>. Now we are ready to tell
MagiSoft to calculate Bill Gates’ birth chart. We do this by clicking the Recalculate Button
located on the furthermost right side of the screen about mid-height. When you click, if your
computer is slow like an early Pentium, an hourglass may appear very briefly to indicate the
280

program is calculating Bill Gates' chart. On fast computers, you will not see an hourglass. When
the program is finished with its calculations, Bill Gates’ Magi AstroChart will appear in the
Graphics Area and all the astrological data in the Scroll Areas and Data Display Area will change
and will display the specifics of his data.
Let’s print out his chart. We do this by opening the File Menu and choosing Print. To
open the File Menu, just point the white arrow of your mouse to the upper left-hand corner of
your screen and point the arrow right on top of the word FILE and click the left mouse button.
You should now see a drop down menu appear. There is a listing on the menu entitled “Print”;
point the mouse to those words until the background of these words turns blue, then click the left
mouse button. A sub-menu will appear and one of the choices in this sub-menu is "Graphics";
you want to select that one by clicking on it. You should now see a new rectangular window in
the middle of your screen that has a horizontal blue bar across the top of the new window. In this
window there is a button that is labeled OK. Point the mouse to the button that says “OK” and
click the left mouse button. You should get a printout of Bill Gates’ Magi AstroChart from your
printer in about 15 seconds.
It is that simple.
For ease of writing, from now on, whenever we say, “click the mouse,” it means, “click
the left mouse button.” When we ask you to enter two keys at the same time, we will just write
“enter [<firstkey> + <secondkey>]”; this means hold down <firstkey> and then press
<secondkey>.
You will notice, of course, that the printout does not have Bill Gates’ name on it; instead
it is entitled “TODAY.” That is because we did not change the name of the chart. Every time
you load MagiSoft v. 2.36, the program will read your computer system’s clock, and give you the
chart for the date, and time of your computer’s internal clock. MagiSoftware also assumes you
are in New York City, so it places “New York City” inside the Place Box, and it puts New York
City’s coordinates into the two boxes for the latitudes and longitudes. Wherever you are, you will
probably want to have an easy way of placing the name and coordinates of your hometown into
the program. Let’s set up the computer to do that.
Point the arrow to the Place Box, click the mouse, and press <Backspace> then type in
the name of the city you live in. If you make a mistake, use the <Backspace> and/or <Delete>
keys to delete the mistakes and re-enter the name of your city. When the name is correct, press
<Tab>. The next box will be blue. It is the box for the latitude; press <Backspace> to erase the
old latitude and enter the latitude of your city using nnNnn or nnSnn depending on where you
are. When you have done this correctly, press <Tab> and the next box will be blue. This is the
box to enter the longitude of your city. Press <Backspace> and enter your city’s longitude using
nnWnn or nnEnn depending on where your city is. When you have done this successfully, press
<Tab> three times. This will have you skip two boxes and the Tz Box should be blue. This is the
Time Zone Box. If you made a mistake and you are not in this box, simply point the mouse to
this box and click the mouse. When your Tz Box is blue, press <Backspace> to erase the old
data, and enter the time zone that you are in. You can enter any number from 0 to 12, or -1 to 12. You do not need to type in the colon or 00. Only use the number keys of your main
keyboard, not the numeric pad. You can add a three letter abbreviation of the time zone after the
time such as “4 EST”; this tells the program to display the letters “EST” after the time zone on all
printouts and on the screen displays. (But adding the “EST" may lengthen the lettering on your
screen and cause an overlap onto part of the Magi AstroChart; if so, leave out the "EST".)

EST
CST
MST

Remember that MagiSoftware uses military time. Also, the time zone is in numeric form:
=5
EDT =4
=6
CDT =5
=7
MDT =6
281

PST

=8
PDT =7
All other time zones also have numeric equivalents from 0 to 12 west of Greenwich, UK
and from -1 to -12 for time zones east of Greenwich, UK.
You can also enter the unusual time zones that use the half-hour, but you must type in the colon.
For example, time zone HST is entered as 10:30.

Once you have entered your time zone, press the <tab> key and point the mouse to the
Recalculate Button and click your mouse. Notice that the data on the upper right hand corner of
the Graphics Area now has your city’s name and coordinates, and time zone. Now let us save all
of this information so we can retrieve it in the future.

SAVING A FILE
To save any data that is on the screen into a file that we can read back, we can use the
standard Windows procedure. You do this first by simply pointing the mouse to the File Menu
(as we did before) and click on the word “File.” A drop down menu should appear. Point the
arrow to “Save”; when the background behind the word “Save” is blue, click the mouse
(remember, always use the left mouse button). Within a second or two of when you click, a new
window will appear. This is the standard Windows Save File window. This new window that
was opened when you clicked “Save” should be rectangular and should have a horizontal blue
band along the top that has the words “Select file to save options in.” Save the file under a name
that makes sense like the name of your city. You can use as many letters in the name as your
Windows operating system allows you. When you have decided on a name, you may simply type
the name and and press the SAVE button. You have now saved a file that has the data for your
city. Your file will be saved with the “ .opt” extension. This means if you typed in the name of
LOSANGELES, the actual name of the file after it is saved will be LOSANGELES.opt. All
MagiSoft programs automatically save files with the extension of " .opt"
READING A FILE
We can now read back the file we just saved. We do this by also using the normal
Windows procedures. When you saved your file, unless you deviated from our instructions, you
saved it in \MAGISOFT, which is the directory your program is in. It is important to know where
your files are.
To read or load a file that you saved, open the File Menu again by using your mouse to
point the mouse to the word “File” at the left upper corner of your screen. Click on it; when you
get the drop down menu, point the mouse to the word “Load” until the background turns blue,
then click the mouse. Another new window should appear in the middle of your screen and it
looks almost exactly like the one that appeared when you clicked “Save” to save the file. This
new window is the Read File Window and will say "Select file to load options from." Simply
click on the file named LOSANGELES.opt. Your hard drive light will blink on and you will see
both Data Grids flash and then provide you with new astrological data. The flashng Data Grids
are an indication that the program made calculations based on the data of the file it just read; on
slow computers, this sometimes take a few seconds and you may feel like the program is
suspended but it is actually reading a file and calculating data for the new file. The program will
make the calculations based on the mode the program was in when the file was saved.
Now you know the very basics of MagiSoft v. 2.36. Please create and save files for your
birth date and a couple of friends or relatives. Experiment with the program’s features. Do not
be afraid. We have thoroughly debugged the program. Besides, you can always turn off the
282

computer and reboot; that will bring you back to the original program’s settings and you will not
lose any of your files.

YOU CAN GO TO FULL SCREEN TO VIEW MORE ASPECTS
When your program is first loaded, it always starts in mode 0. You can tell this because
the number “0” appears inside the Mode Box. There are twelve modes and each mode makes
different calculations and gives you different types of data in the Left and Middle Grid Areas.
We want to go to mode 1 which displays the natal aspects. You do that by entering [<Alt> +
<1>]. The two Data Grid Areas will blink and display new data. Now, the data in the Left Data
Grid are the natal aspects for the Chart Date in the longitudes. The declinational aspects are in
the Middle Data Grid.
When you look at the Data Grids, you will see only some of the data because there is a
window and the window is not large enough to show you all the data. You can see the rest of the
data by using the <Page down> and <Page up> keys, along with the four arrow keys. You can
also click on the Scroll Buttons as shown on Grid Diagrams One and Two earlier in this manual.
Play with each of these keys and see how they work on the data behind the window of the Left
and Middle Data Grids.
No matter how you use the scroll controls, you cannot see enough of the data all at once.
For this reason, we gave you a way to have a much larger window. Enter [<Ctrl> + <G>]. You
will go to the FULL GRAPHICS SCREEN and get a full screen of the Magi AstroChart plus
much more viewable data. On the right side of the screen there is a very large window that has all
the data behind the small window of the Left Data Grid. This large window is called the FULL
SCREEN GRID. It always contains whatever data is in the Left Data Grid of the Main Screen.
Depending on the size of your computer screen, the Full Screen Grid is big enough to let you
view 35 to 65 aspects at the same time. But there are times when it is still not big enough to see
all the data at once. If you press the <Page Down> key, the data will scroll. And the <Page Up>
key will scroll the data back up.

HOW TO RESIZE WINDOWS
You can change the size of the Full Screen Grid in the same way you do with the
windows of other software programs. If you do not know how to do this, check with a friend or
your Windows manuals. But very quickly, you can adjust the size of the Full Screen Grid by
pointing the mouse at any of the four corners of the window. For example, move the arrow of
your mouse to the upper left corner of the window. Move it around this corner very slowly until
you see the white arrow disappear and a black double-arrow appear. There are two types of black
double-arrows; one type points to the left and right, and the other type points diagonally. These
black double-arrows are called RESIZING ARROWS. When either type of resizing Arrows
appear, HOLD DOWN THE LEFT MOUSE BUTTON and at the same time move the mouse to
your left. You should see the Full Screen Aspects Window become larger. Let go of the mouse
button when you have made the window the size you want. To decrease the size of the window,
point the arrow at the upper left corner and move the arrow slowly around the small corner area
until you see one of the Resizing Arrows appear. Hold down the left mouse button and move
your mouse to the right until the window is the size you want.
Remember there are two types of Resizing Arrows. One type has black arrows pointing
diagonally and the other has black arrows pointing to the right and left. When you get a diagonal

283

Resizing Arrow, you can change both the height and width of the window; the other arrows only
allow you to change the width. You can get diagonal Resizing Arrows to appear at any of the
four corners of the window. The left-right Resizing Arrows appear when you point the white
arrow along the vertical borders of the window. By using the Resizing Arrows, you can make the
Full Screen Grid any size you want.
If you point the arrow to any part of the blue bar at the top of the window and hold down
the left mouse button, the whole window will move wherever you move your mouse.
And if you want to see the Magi AstroChart in total without the Full Screen Grid, just
enter [<Ctrl> + <A>]. The Full Screen Grid will disappear. To make it reappear, use the same
hotkey combination and enter [<Ctrl> + <A>] again.
You can resize the Full Screen Grid in any of the twelve modes.

HOW TO GO FROM MODE TO MODE IN THE FULL GRAPHICS
SCREEN
Let’s go back to the Main Screen. We do that by entering [<Ctrl> + <G>]. This is the
same combination of keys we used to go from the Main Screen to the Full Graphics Screen in the
first place. (When a hotkey brings you back and forth from one screen to another, the hotkey is
said to TOGGLE between two screens.) We should be back to the Main Screen. Now let us tell
the program to include the Moon in all our calculations. Please find the Moon Box and make
sure there is a check mark in that box; if there isn’t, point the white arrow to the box and click the
mouse. A check mark should appear.
Please go back to the Full Graphics Screen by entering [<Ctrl> + <G>] again. You
should be back to a full screen of the Magi AstroChart and a Full Screen Grid will cover most of
the right side of the chart. The Full Graphics Screen always contains the Full Screen Grid when
you first change screens.
We should still be in mode 1. As you can see from the description of the modes (in the
earlier section about modes entitled "There are Twelve Modes"), mode 1 lists all natal aspects and
it lists the longitudinal ones in the Left Data Grid. But in Full Graphics Screen, there is no Left or
Middle Data Grid; there is just one Full Screen Grid, so we put whatever is supposed to be in the
Left Data Grid into the Full Screen Grid. In mode 1, this window has the longitudinal aspects.
We can make the window list the declinational aspects by going to mode 2. Let’s go to mode 2;
we do that by entering [<Alt> + <2>]. You will now see the declinational aspects in the Full
Screen Grid. Remember you can resize the window and page up and down.
Now let’s go to mode 3 which lists the midpoints of the planets. Enter [<Alt> + <3>]. A
listing of midpoints will appear in the Full Screen Grid. Note the order that the midpoints are
listed. The first midpoint to be listed is the Sun/Moon midpoint but there is no listing for the
Moon/Sun midpoint because they are the same. However, there are times when you want to have
all the midpoints of a particular planet grouped together, such as all Saturn midpoints or all
Jupiter midpoints. We can do that with your MagiSoft program. But we have to set a switch in
the Data Entry Area. Go back to the Main Screen by entering [<Ctrl> + <G>]. You should have
the Main Screen back. Now find the box that is labeled “All Comb”; this box is located just
above the VT box, which in turn is just to the left of the Chiron (CH) box. Put a check mark in
this box by pointing the arrow to it and click the mouse. An hourglass will appear briefly and the
Left Data Grid will blink and display new data. Go back to Full Graphics Screen by entering
[<Ctrl> + <G>]. You should be in Full Screen Graphics. The Full Screen Grid will now have a
listing of both the Sun/Moon midpoint and the Moon/Sun midpoint. If you scroll down you will
see that all the Saturn midpoints are now listed together.

284

PRINTING ASPECT LISTINGS
All printing must be done from the Main Screen. Therefore we must first go back to the
Main Screen by entering [<Ctrl> + <G>]. To do any printing, we need to open the File Menu; we
already learned how to use the mouse to do that when we learned how to save and read a file.
Just point the mouse to the upper left hand corner of your screen at the word “File” and click the
mouse. The File Menu drop-down window should appear in the upper left hand corner of your
screen. Click on "Print" and then click on "Aspects" in the sub-menus. You should get the Print
Window we already learned about; simply click the OK button in the Print Window and the
aspects will be printed.
(The program will only print what fits on one page. If the number of aspects you are
printing does not fit on one page, look at the Left Data Grid and use the <Page Down> button to
scroll down to the last aspect that was printed. Then repeat the print procedure; the program will
print the aspects beginning with the aspect you scrolled down to. But you rarely have to do this
because 99% of the time, all the aspects fit on one page.)
You can also customize the Magi AstroChart so that it displays and prints only the aspect
lines you want to include. We will use an example below to explain how to do this.

ANOTHER EXAMPLE OF CREATING A CHART
Our example is Alanis Morissette, who was born 6/1/1974. Please click the ENTER
DATA button. The Date Box should become blue; enter <Backspace> and then type in
“6/1/1974” and press <Tab>. Now the Time Box is blue; press <Backspace> and enter “12”,
then press <Tab>; this tells the program to calculate the data based on a birth time of noon,
because we do not know her exact time of birth. The Time Zone (Tz) Box should now be blue;
press <Backspace> and enter <4> and press <Tab> again. We have just instructed the program
to make its calculations based on the time zone of 4:00, which is EDT. Now point the mouse to
the far right side of the Name Box and click. There should be a blinking cursor in the Name Box.
Use <Backspace> to erase whatever is in the Name Box and type in “Alanis Morissette.” Press
<Tab> four times. The Place Box should now be blue with a blinking cursor at the furthest left
part of the box indicating it is ready to accept data that you type in. (You could have also simply
clicked on the Place Box instead of tabbing 4 time.) Now press <Backspace> until you erase
whatever is in the Place Box. Type in “Ottawa, Canada.” This is all the data we need to enter.
The geographic coordinates and exact time of birth are not always necessary in Magi Astrology.
In this case, we can leave them out. It is better to have them but they are not always known and
Magi Astrology can provide very accurate interpretations without them.
At this point, we are ready to create Morissette’s chart. But we need to turn off the Exact
Feature. We do not want the Exact Box to have a check mark in it. If there is a check mark in the
Exact Box, remove it by pointing the mouse to the box and click the mouse. We will learn about
the Exact Feature shortly, but when it is turned on, it makes millions of additional calculations
and slows down all the features of the program so we want it turned off for what we are about to
do. There are some other features we also do not need right now. Since we do not know Alanis’
exact time of birth, we cannot correctly calculate her ascendant and midheaven, or vertex. The
AC/MC box controls whether the program will calculate the ascendant and midheaven and
whether these two calculated points will be included in every calculation. Turn this feature off by
making sure there is no check mark in the AC/MC Box. For the purposes of this example, we
also want to turn off the Vertex Box, the NN Box, the Moon Box, and also TURN OFF THE
CHIRON BOX so make sure there is no check mark in any of these boxes. If there is a check
mark in any of those boxes, point the arrow to the box and click the mouse.

285

We are now ready to tell the program to create Alanis’ chart. To do so, point the mouse
to the Recalculate Button (located at the farthest right part of the screen, and in the middle level)
and click. The program should recalculate all data and create Alanis’ Magi AstroChart. (You can
also tell the MagiSoft program to recalculate by entering [<Ctrl> + <C>] or use the Commands
Menu and the choose Recalculate.)

HOW TO CALCULATE MAGI QUADS
Now let’s learn how to calculate the Magi Quads for Alanis. We can tell the program to
calculate her Magi Quads by going to mode 4. Please enter [<Alt> + <4>]. This tells the
program to go to mode 4, which calculates all Magi Quads and lists the longitudinal ones in the
Left Data Grid, while listing the declinational Magi Quads in the Middle Data Grid. Below is
what your Data Grids should look like:

Figure 127 magi quads

Please remember that the <Page Up> and <Page Down> keys work only on the data in
the Left Data Grid. We had said earlier that only the Left Data Grid actually scrolls. We need to
clarify that statement. The <Page Dn> and <Page Up> keys work only on the Left Data Grid. If
you want to scroll the data in the Middle Data Grid, you can follow these instructions: Look at the
lower right hand corner of the Middle Data Grid; there is a very small box (a Scroll Button) with
a tiny arrow pointing down; point the white arrow of your mouse on this box and click. The data
in the Middle Data Grid will move. There are other boxes that are the same size as the one you
just clicked with little arrows in them. Each one moves the data behind the nearest window.
Every Data Grid has these SCROLL BUTTONS. Please find them and click on each to see what
they do.
Now let us learn how to draw lines to connect the MQs. When you first enter [<Alt> +
<4>] and calculate MQs, the MagiAstrochart will have a whole lot of lines. Press <F1> to make
all these lines disappear. In both the Left and Middle Grid Areas, note that the leftmost vertical
column is shaded, and all the other columns are white. In the left-most box of the highest
horizontal column that is shaded, there is an asterisk that looks like this: *. This box is called the
Asterisk Marker Box. Beneath this box is a column of shaded boxes that are empty. Point your
mouse’s arrow to the shaded box just below the Asterisk Marker Box and click the mouse. An
asterisk will appear in the box you just clicked and the Graphics Area will change and draw in
four lines. These lines connect the planets that make up the Magi Quad that is listed in the
horizontal row immediately to the right of the box you just clicked. You can erase the lines by
clicking the box again. Please do that and note that the asterisk is gone and so are the lines.
Each MQ is listed to read horizontally and each MQ is numbered. That is why the first
vertical column to the right of the shaded column has the numbers 1, 2, 3, 4, 5.... etc. If you press
286

<Page Down> until the data stops scrolling down, you will see that for Alanis, the last MQ listed
in the Left Data Grid is numbered 16. This means Alanis has 16 important Magi Quads in the
longitudes. Now press <Page Up> several times until the data does not scroll up any more. You
are back to the original position.
Please enter [<Ctrl> + <G>]; you are now in Full Screen Graphics and the Full Aspects
Window shows you all of the 16 MQs all at once. Everyone's most important MQs are the ones
numbered 1 to 6. This is usually the case; the most important MQs are the ones listed first using
the Magi Sequences. She has two Jup/Plu MQs in the longitudes and the second one is (Jup +
Plu) <> (Sun + Mer), which means super success as a singer. The first MQ is (Jup + Plu) <>
(Sun + Sat). (When two MQs share three component planets, there is a conjuncted MQ.) Notice
that in the Left Data Grid, underneath the shaded box with the letters “Asp” in it, there is a
column of boxes with the number “180” in them. The “Asp” stands for “aspect” and the 180
means opposition. In the first horizontal row, to the left of the number “180” are the glyphs for
Jup/Plu and to the right of the number “180” are the glyphs for Sun/Mer. To the right of that is
“a2.56.” All together, this row of data stands for a Jup/Plu opposition of Sun/Mer with an orb of
2.56 degrees and the aspect is applying (denoted by the “a”). Jup/Plu means the midpoint of
Jupiter and Pluto. When the midpoint of Jupiter and Pluto is opposed to the midpoint of Sun and
Mercury, a Magi Quad is created.
You can also create Magi Quads with a conjunction of midpoints. Press <Page Down>
and note that in the Left Data Grid, in the “Asp” column, there is the number “000” from the
ninth to the 16th Magi Quads. This means that those Magi Quads are produced by a conjunction
of midpoints. When a Magi Quad is produced by a conjunction, all four planets are on the same
half of the 360-degree circle; if an opposition creates a Magi Quad, two planets are on one half of
the circle, and the other two planets are in the other half. Both types of Magi Quads are
interpreted in the same way.
Now let us go through how we read the data for each mode. Go to mode 1 by entering
[<Alt> + <1>]. In the Left Data Grid, there are planetary glyphs and numbers but the first aspect
listed is Sun 180 Nep which means the Sun is opposed by Neptune. The orb is 2.60 degrees and
the aspect is separating (denoted by the “s”). The second aspect is Sun 45 Mars, which means the
Sun is semi-square Mars. The third aspect is Sun 135 Ura, which means that the Sun and Uranus
form a sesqui-quadrate. MagiSoftware lists all aspects including these odd aspects because some
astrologers are very interested in them.
In the mode that we are in, the declinational aspects are listed in the Middle Data Grid.
We should see that Alanis has Sun parallel Mars and the aspect is only 0.34 degrees apart and is
applying.
Now let’s see how mode 6 works. Enter [<Alt> + <6>]. This mode gives you all the
Midpoint Crossings. In the Left Data Grid, the first Midpoint Crossing listed (number 1) is “Sun
000 Ven/ Mars a2.76” meaning that the Sun is conjunct the midpoint of Venus/Mars and this
aspect is applying with an orb of 2.76 degrees. (Depending on the size of your computer screen,
you might have to use the horizontal scroll button to see all the data about the orb.) Scroll down
to the Midpoint Crossing numbered 10, which says “Mer 180 Jup/Ura a0.88.” This means that
the 10th listed MDX is Mercury opposed by the Jupiter/Uranus midpoint and it is applying with
an orb of 0.88 degrees. But remember that the opposition is the same as a conjunction with
Midpoint Crossings because of our law of Midpoint Equivalence (explained beginning on page
29 of the Magi Society Ephemeris). In either case, this MDX represents success in entertainment
and fame (Jup/Ura) in singing (Mercury).
Look at Alanis’ declinational Midpoint Crossings that are listed in the Middle Data Grid.
The second one is Venus paralleled by the Mer/Jup midpoint, signifying money (Venus) from
success in singing (Mer/Jup).
With all aspects, in any mode, you can pick out which aspects you want to draw lines for.
Just point the mouse to the shaded box to the left of the aspect and click the mouse. An asterisk
287

will appear and so will the lines for that aspect. If you want to erase all aspect lines that you
selected (or the program drew), enter [<Alt> + <O>] (this is the letter O, not the number 0).
If you use the Print Graphics selection in the File Menu (the way we already explained)
the program will print the Magi AstroChart with all of the aspect lines you selected.

CALCULATING TRANSITS AND DISPLAYING RED FLASHING
PLANETS
Our next step is to learn how to calculate transits. The example we will use is O.J.
Simpson, who was born July 9, 1947. Click the ENTER DATA button. The Date Box should be
blue; press <Backspace> to erase the old data and enter “7/9/1947.” Then press <Tab>.
Although many astrologers have published Simpson’s birth chart with an exact time, we do not
usually need it in Magi Astrology because we can do enough without it. The Time Box is preset
at “12:00” and the Time Zone Box (Tz) is at “4:00.” Those settings are fine and we will not
change them. Point the arrow to the middle of the Name Box, and click. The blinking cursor
should appear. This time the cursor appears in the middle of the name that is in the Name Box (in
this case “Alanis Morissette”) because we pointed the arrow to the middle of the box. Use both
the <Delete> and <Backspace> keys to erase the data; then enter “OJ Simpson.” Go to mode 1
by entering [<Alt> + <1>]. The program will now recalculate and provide the data for mode 1;
whenever you change modes, the program recalculates based on the data and switches in the Data
Entry Area.
We are not going to talk about Simpson’s chart itself; we are only using him as an
example for transits. Your MagiSoft v. 2.36 has capabilities of calculating and displaying
transits that are more advanced than any other astrology program. Let us see what
Simpson’s transits were on the day of Nicole Simpson’s murder, June 12, 1994, around 10:30
PM, PDT.
The first step is to open the COMPARISON Window, which is the window to enter data
for the day you want to calculate transits for. You do this by clicking the CREATE CAC menu,
and then selecting BIRTH DATA FOR RED PLANETS by clicking on that. A new window will
appear in the middle of the bottom of your screen. It is the Comparison Window. On some
computer systems, the bottom of this window may not be fully viewable. If this is the case, we
can move the window up to see the bottom of the window. To move the window up, point the
mouse to any spot on the blue bar at the top of the Comparison Window, hold down your left
mouse button and move the mouse up an inch. This should move the window. Now let go of the
mouse.
Note that across the top of the Comparison Window, there is a blue bar. This is called the
Title Bar. Below this Title Bar, on the left side, there are two tabs marked “natal” and
“comparison.” Each tab marks the label of a file folder. If you point the mouse and click on the
tab with “natal,” you will bring the Natal File Folder to the front and you will see that Simpson’s
birth data are in the boxes of that folder. Now click on the tab that says “comparison”; Simpson’s
data is now behind the Comparison File Folder. The Comparison File Folder has boxes for you
to enter the day and time of day that you want MagiSoft to use to calculate transits. When you
first open the Comparison File Folder, it will have data like “Today” in all of its boxes but you
can change them all.
Let’s see what Simpson’s transits were on the night of Nicole Simpson’s murder. The
murder took place on June 12, 1994, around 10:30 PM. Click on the Date Box of the comparison
folder. If anything was in the box it will turn blue and you must enter <Backspace> to erase the
old data. If nothing was in the box, a blinking cursor will appear at the beginning of the box.

288

Enter “6/12/1994.” All the boxes in the comparison folder work just like the ones in the Data
Entry Area. Use the same procedures to enter the time of 10:30 PM (2230 military time) and
enter “22.30”. Now enter “7” in the Zone Box which is for the time zone. Also enter “Wife
murdered” in the Name Box. When you have completed these entries, click the DONE Button at
the bottom of the Comparison window; the window should disappear. You can get it back any
time by clicking the Comparison Button.
Please make sure all of the Check Boxes are turned off!
We are now ready to calculate transits. You tell MagiSoft to calculate transits by going
to mode 8. Tell MagiSoft that you want to calculate Simpson’s transits on June 12, 1994 by
entering [<Alt> + <8>]. You will see the customary blinking of the Data Grid Areas. Scroll
down to the transit that is numbered 38 that is in the Left Data Grid; that transit says “Saturn 150
Pluto s0.14” which means that transiting Saturn was 150 degrees from Simpson’s natal Pluto on
June 12, 1994. As we learned in Astrology Really Works!, this is a very important transit and is
one of the worst you can have.
But it is a pain in the neck to scroll through a large list to find this transit, listed 38th. We
designed the program to make it easy to find any type of transit. We can overlay the
transiting planets and make them flash in red, and then tell the program to draw lines to
connect only a specific type of transits.
To do all that, you need to create a CAC and make the transiting planets flash in red. As
the first step, click the CREATE CAC menu, and select OVERLAY RED PLANETS. You will
get a new window labeled “Planets to Overlay”; this is the Overlay Window. In this window,
there is a vertical column with all of the planetary glyphs and the abbreviations of the
corresponding planets. For now, point the mouse to the word “Sat”, then PRESS AND HOLD
DOWN the Control Key and AT THE SAME TIME click the left mouse button; the background
behind the word will turn blue. This tells the program that you want to display the position of
transiting Saturn on Simpson’s natal chart. (We can do this with any combination of planets that
you like, or all of them. The procedure of holding down the control key and clicking is the
standard procedure for Windows programs.) Close the Overlay Window by clicking the OK
button in the window. In the Graphics Area you will now easily see the transiting positions of
Saturn because it is flashing in red, for both the longitudes and the declinations.
Let’s now display all of the transiting planets in flashing red. To do this, you need to
again click on the CREATE CAC menu and select Overlay Red Planets. Now when the Overlay
Window opens, click on all of the planets (Sun through Chiron) in the Overlay Window to turn
blue. You can do this by holding down the <Ctrl key> and clicking each planet until they are all
blue. Then close the window by clicking the OK button. You will see that every transiting planet
is now displayed and flashes in red. The display in this form is very helpful; but it is still not
really easy to pick out the important transits. But MagiSoft has a way of doing that. We use the
four function keys F9 to F12, as follows:
Press F9. All transits that are quincunxes will be highlighted with aspect lines.
Press F10. All transits that are trines or sextiles will be highlighted with aspect lines.
Press F11. All transits that are oppositions or squares will be highlighted with aspect
lines.
Press F12. All transits that are quintiles or biquintiles will be highlighted with aspect
lines.
In each case, the program will draw the transits by connecting the transiting planet to the
natal planet. (Or you can use the SELECT LINE ANGLES menu and click on any of the
choices.)
The reason we use the name Comparison File Folder rather than Transit File Folder is
that you can use the same folder to enter data for doing chart comparisons with a Connected
Person; the calculations of transits is exactly the same as the calculations of INTERASPECTS
289

between two people. If you want to see what interaspects you make to anyone, use the same
procedures as we just showed you. But put your own birth data in the Data Entry Area (or the
Natal File Folder), and enter the birth data of the person you want to compare yourself to in the
Comparison File Folder. More about this later.
Getting back to the transits of Simpson, we can tell MagiSoft to highlight all aspects by
any single planet, like Saturn. To do this, first we want to erase all aspect lines; do that by
entering [<Alt> + <O>] (the letter O, not the number zero). This hotkey combination can always
erase aspect lines that you may not want. To display all aspect lines by only Saturn, point the
mouse arrow to the Auto/A Box and click. (This box is in the Data Entry Area, on the fifth row
of boxes and has “99” in it everytime you load MagiSoft.) Remove the “99” by backspacing and
then enter the number “6” into the box and click the Recalculate Button. The program will now
display every aspect that is made by transiting Saturn, along with every transiting aspect to natal
Saturn. To not display the aspects to natal Saturn, simply turn off the other planets. You do that
by opening the Overlay Window (enter [<Ctrl> + <V>]) and click all the other planets to turn
them off (make them not blue). When only Sat is displayed in a blue background, turn off the
window by clicking on the box with the “X” in the upper right hand corner of the Overlay
Window. You now have on display only the aspects by transiting Saturn. In the Left Data Grid,
these aspects are highlighted with an asterisk.
To get Saturn aspects, we entered the number “6” in the Auto/A Box. Here are the codes
for the other planets: Sun=0, Mer=1, Ven=2, Moon=3, Mars=4, Jup=5, Sat=6, Ura=7, Nep=8,
Plu=9, Chi=11, Node=12, ascendent=17, midheaven=18, vertex=19. For example, if you want
only aspects by Jupiter, enter “5” in the Auto/A Box, and click the Recalculate Button. But you
must also display Jupiter in flashing red or the program will not show the aspect lines by Jupiter.
You can print any table of transiting aspects, or graphics by using the print functions
under the File Menu. If you have a full function color printer, the printer will print the flashing
red planets and aspect lines. Otherwise the transiting planets will be printed in a black halftone
with a rectangle around them to distinguish them from the natal planets.

THE EXACT FEATURE
The exact feature is unique to MagiSoft and is one of its most useful features. This
feature calculates the day and time that any aspect, or transit, becomes exact. Please check your
screen and see if this feature is turned on by finding the Exact Box and looking to see if there is a
check mark in this box. If not, turn the feature on by pointing the mouse to the Exact Box and
click the mouse; a check mark will appear indicating this feature is now turned on. Whenever
you turn on or turn off the Exact Box, the program will recalculate automatically without your
having to click the Recalculate Button.
Please go to full screen mode; enter [<Ctrl> + <G>]. You should see the Full Screen
Aspects Window; enlarge this window and drag the left part of the window further left until the
last two columns show completely. These two columns are entitled “Exact” and “Exact-Time.”
The Exact Column tells you the time to exactness of the aspect; it can be measured in days, hours,
and minutes. The Exact-Time Column tells you the actual date and hour that the aspect was last
exact, or will be exact. The actual time of day is calculated using the time zone you set in the Tz.
Box of the Data Entry Area. There may be a plus or minus indicator after the date to specify the
range of accuracy for the projected date.
The Exact feature also works in all other modes. For example, in mode 4 the exact
feature tells you when the Magi Quads are exact.
You should turn off the Exact feature when you are not interested in such data because it
slows down the program. Calculating exact times requires millions of manipulations.

290

SORTING BY TIME TO EXACT
It is very often useful to be able to list the aspects (including transiting aspects) in order
of the time when the aspect will be exact. This is especially useful in financial astrology when
we want to analyze alignments during a day. And it is crucial for transiting aspects. For these
reasons, your MagiSoft program has a special hotkey combination that allows you to sort all
aspects based on time to exact. Simply enter [<Alt> + <Q>]. This hotkey combination tells the
MagiSoft program how to list the aspects. One way is to list by Magi Sequences or by planet
group; the other is by time to exactness of the aspect. The [<Alt> + <Q>] hotkey combination
toggles the sorting order from one to the other. Go ahead and enter those keys in each of the
twelve different modes (listed in the earlier section entitled "There are Twelve Modes") and see
what we mean.

MAGISOFT HAS A TIME ORB FILTER
Another very useful feature unique to MagiSoft is the Time Orb Filter. If you enter
[<Ctrl> + <O>], the letter O and not the number 0, you will open a pop-up window that allows
you to enter a time orb. After you enter the number of degrees for the Time Orb, you must press
<tab> and then you must tell the MagiSoft program to apply this new orb by clicking the little
box that is labeled "Enable Time Orb Filter" so that there is a little check mark in the box; finally
you still have to click the OK button in the Time Orb Window. Once you activate this, you will
obtain a listing of only the aspects that are within the time orb you set. Please bear in mind that
this is a time orb, not an orb in degrees. (The orbs in degrees are set using one of the two Orb
Boxes in the Data Entry Area.) DO NOT FORGET THAT YOU ARE USING A TIME
ORB. Whenever you activate the Time Orb filter, please remember that you have done so
because all of the listing of the aspects and interaspects will change and you will get a list reduced
to only those aspects within your time orb. THIS IS A FABULOUSLY USEFUL FEATURE
BUT UNLESS YOU ARE DOING SERIOUS RESEARCH INTO TIME ORBS, WE SUGGEST
YOU AVOID USING THIS FEATURE BECAUSE YOU ARE LIKELY TO FORGET TO
TURN IT OFF AND THE PROGRAM WILL HAVE MANY FEWER ASPECTS.

THE CTRL + N HOT KEY
Everyone needs to look at the astrological chart of the current date and time on a very regular
basis. For this reason we provide you with a hotkey so you can easily obtain the chart for the
current time and date. Simply enter [<Ctrl> + <N>]. MagiSoftware will automatically read your
computer's date and time and transfer the data to the screen and recalculate and update all the
astrological data and chart for you.

TIME INCREMENT

291

When calculating transits, it is very useful to be able to advance or go back a specific
number of days or hours. MagiSoftware lets you easily do this by allowing you to preset an
INCREMENT. On the first line of the screen display, the last box serves this purpose, and is
called the Dt. Box; this box is followed by two very small boxes with the "+/-" symbols. It is
preset to one day and reads "1d.” To advance the Chart Date and all the astrological data by one
day, hold down the <Ctrl> key and press the <right arrow> key. The date in the Date Box will be
changed to the next day, and all the data will also be changed accordingly. To go back a day,
simply hold down the <Ctrl> key and press the <back arrow>. You can also click on the “+/-”
boxes that are just to the right of the Dt. Box. If you click the “+” Button, the data will be
increased by the Increment; if you click the “-” Button, the data will be decreased by the
Increment.
You can set the Increment to as many as 9999 days (enter "9999d") or to as little as .01
seconds (enter " .01s"). You can only enter days, hours, minutes, or seconds; "h" is used for
hours. You must enter a number followed by d, h, m, or s. The program automatically converts
certain times that you might enter. For example, if you enter "90m", and press <enter>, the
program will convert it to "1.5h".
In modes 0 to 7, when you use the Increment to forward or reverse (using <Ctrl> and the
right or left arrow keys), there will be a change in the Date Box of the Data Entry Area. But
when you are in modes 8 or 9 (transit modes), the increment is added or subtracted from the date
that is displayed in the Comparison File Folder of the Comparison Window. This allows you to
view the changes in the transits from day to day. This is another very useful feature, as we will
see in the next demonstration.

CALCULATING AND DISPLAYING YOUR OWN TRANSITS
Let us say you want to check your transits for each of the next ten days. We can very
easily do this with MagiSoft v. 2.36. To do so, follow these steps:
You should have already created a file with your birth data as we suggested. If not,
please do so now. Then load your file using the procedure we already taught you. Click on the
Comparison Button; you will get the Comparison Window. If the bottom of the Comparison
Window is not visible, click and hold on the Title Bar and drag it up an inch so the whole window
is visible. There are three buttons on the right side of the Comparison Window and they are
labeled ‘now’, ‘clear’ and ‘load’. Point the mouse to the NOW Button and click the mouse. You
will see that today’s date and time will appear in the boxes of the Comparison File Folder.
(Assuming that your computer’s system clock is accurate.) Now click the DONE button. To
calculate your transits, enter [<Alt> + <8>]. All your transits are now listed in the Scroll Areas.
But it is much easier if you can actually see the transiting planets flash in red on the screen. To do
this, click on the CREATE CAC menu and select Ovelay Red Planets by clicking on it (you can
also enter [<Ctrl> + <V>] to open the Overlay Window), click on all the planets until they are all
blue (remember you must hold down the <Ctrl key> when you click or unclick a planet) and close
the window by clicking the OK button in the window. (We suggest that you do not click on the
midheaven, ascendant or vertex since they do not appear to be important in creating transits.)
You should see all the transiting planets overlaid and flashing in red. Now let’s go to full screen
by entering [<Ctrl> + <G>]. Let’s see the whole chart without the Full Screen Grid; hide that
window by entering [<Ctrl> + <A>]. You now have an unobstructed look at your chart, with
declinations and all the transiting planets flashing in red. Now draw all transiting oppositions and
squares by pressing <F11>. All oppositions and squares aspect lines will be drawn. If you have
important transiting planets making oppositions and/or squares to crucial natal planets, you have
to be especially careful.

292

Now check your transits for tomorrow by entering [<Ctrl> + <Right Arrow>]. Note that
the date in the upper right corner changes to tomorrow’s date. You can also use <F9>, <F10>
and <F12> to screen for other angles of transits. When you use any of the four function keys
(<F9>-<F12>), the Full Screen Grid will show only the aspects that you screen for. For example,
in <F11>, the only transits listed will be oppositions and squares. Check this out by bringing
back the Full Screen Grid; you do that by entering [<Ctrl> +<A>]. If you want a full listing of
the transiting aspects, enter <F1>. All the aspect lines will disappear but the Full Screen Grid
will have all of the transiting aspects, in the longitudes. If you want the declinational transiting
aspects, go to mode 9 by entering [<Alt> + <9>]. This will display the declinational transits in
the Full Screen Grid and if you go back to the Main Screen by entering [<Ctrl> + <G>] again, the
declinational transiting aspects are now listed in the Left Data Grid of the Main Screen. When
you are in mode 9, the <F9>-<F12> functions are inoperative since they are designed only for the
longitudes, so always enter F1 before going to mode 9.
SPECIAL FEATURES FOR FINANCIAL AND ELECTIONAL ASTROLOGY

SEARCHING FOR GRAND TRINES AND T-SQUARES
One of the best uses of the Time Increment is to use it in conjunction with the AUTO
SEARCH features of the program so as to find the next day that there will be a grand trine, or Tsquare, etc. Let us show you how this works.
Assuming that you are where we left off in checking for your transits, we need to turn off
all the overlay planets. You do this by entering [<Ctrl> + <V>] to open the Overlay Window and
then click off all the planets and close the Overlay Window. The red flashing planets should all
be gone. (Occasionally, with some computer systems, for some reason, one or more planets will
still be flashing. If this happens, you need to repeat the procedure of shutting off the flashing red
planets. We also programmed in a special hotkey combination that toggles the red flashing
planets on and off. If you have the red planets working, you can remove them by entering [<Alt>
+ <V>]. If you re-enter this hotkey combination, you get the red planets back.) With the red
planets turned off, out next step is to go to mode 1 which is the mode that displays the aspects of
a day. We do that by entering [<Alt> + <1>]. Now we are ready to search for the day that has
the next T-square. We want to first display the chart for today’s date and time and go forward
from there; to do that please enter the hotkey combination of [<Ctrl> + <N>]. You should see
today’s chart. The increment should be set to 1.0d. To search for T-squares, press F11. If there
are squares or oppositions, the planets that form them will have aspect lines connecting them, and
since T-squares are formed by squares and oppositions, they will now show up. To check
tomorrow’s chart, enter <Ctrl> + <Right-arrow>. You will now see the next day’s data. You
may find this process slow if the Exact function was left on; you can speed the program up by
turning off the Exact function. Click the Exact Box if it has a check mark in it. Now keep hitting
<Ctrl> + <Right-arrow> until you find a T-square; this may take a while. But you can see the
function working. When there is a T-square, it will get displayed. <F10> will search for all
trines and sextiles and display a grand trine whenever it occurs.

AUTO SEARCH AND HIGHLIGHTING
This is an option that allows you to designate to the MagiSoftware program the planet
you are interested in highlighting. For example, suppose you want to easily pick out all of the

293

Magi Quads that include Venus. You can do that. Simply point the mouse and click the mouse
on the Auto/A Box. The "Auto/A" is an abbreviation for "Auto Search for planet A.” Erase the
"99" that is in this box by entering the number "2" and press <Tab>. If you now enter [<Alt> +
4] to get longitudinal Magi Quads, every Magi Quad that has Venus as a component planet
should now be highlighted by an asterisk in the Scroll Areas, and each Venus Magi Quad is also
displayed in the Graphics Area. You can also use the Increment to see how the Magi Quads
change day to day by entering [<Ctrl> + <Right Arrow>].
If you are interested in only Venus + Uranus pairings of Magi Quads, then change the
data in the box to the right of the Auto/A Box (marked just "B" and is an abbreviation for "Auto
Search for Planet B"). Right now, the box have "99"; change it to "7" and then press <Tab>.
Now only Venus + Uranus MQs are highlighted with an asterisk.
For the Auto Search option, each planet is assigned a code, like 2 for Venus and 7 for
Uranus. The code for each planet is the same as the ones we just listed for you at the end of the
section entitled “Calculating Transits and Displaying Red Flashing Planets.” But the code is also
on your screen. Notice that the first column of numbers on the farthest left side of the Data
Display Area has the numbers 0 to 19. These are the codes for the planets; each number
represents a planet for the purposes of using the Auto Search. Use "0" for the Sun, "1" for
Mercury, "2" for Venus, etc. If you do not want to select any planet to auto search for, you need
to set both the "Auto/A" and the "B" fields back to "99". ALWAYS REMEMBER THIS. Now
please reset both Auto/A and /B to "99". The "99" code tells the MagiSoftware to not select any
planet for auto highlighting.
Those of you who want to know if Magi Quads can be comprised of Ascendants and
Midheavens will have a lot of fun by entering "18" and/or "19" in the Auto Search Fields. Have
fun. They work! Midheavens and ascendants can be very important components of Magi Quads
and Midpoint Crossings.

ADJUSTING THE ORBS
It is important to be able to change the orbs (in degrees) that you are interested in using.
This way, you can actually determine what the effective orb of a particular aspect is by checking
a number of research subjects who have the same aspect but very different orbs. You can set one
orb for the longitudinal aspects while setting another orb for the declinational aspects.
The box labeled “Orb:” is to set the orb for longitudinal aspects; it has the number “3” in it now.
The box labeled “Orb/d:” is to set the orb for declinational aspects; it has the number “1” in it
now.
Play with the orbs and see what it does. Note that when you change an orb, you must
click the Recalculate Button for the new orb to take effect. The larger the orb that you use, the
more aspects you will get in all listings.
There is a theory in Magi Astrology that postulates that the more exact an orb of a natal
aspect, the more important that aspect is to the native. The theory continues by proposing that the
most valuable talents that the native is born with are the ones defined by the most exact aspects.
Especially MDXs and MQs. You now have the ability to check this theory out for yourself. The
exactness of an aspect can be measured in both time and distance. In other words, the exactness
of an aspect can be measured in time orb and in degrees. MagiSoft is the only program in the
world that gives you both. The Magi Society has been doing research using time and distance

294

orbs for centuries and we know that the most exact aspects are the most significant. Now with
MagiSoft, you can see this theory work for yourself.

SCREENING FOR APPLYING ASPECTS ONLY
It is also useful in research to distinguish if a birth aspect is applying or separating.
Although you can obtain this information by checking the already available data, you might want
a listing of only applying aspects. To do this, all you have to do is point the mouse at the
AppOnly Box and click until a check mark is in the box. Here too, you must click the
Recalculate Button for the feature to be in effect. BUT PLEASE DO NOT FORGET TO
CHANGE THE AppOnly BOX BACK TO A BLANK (NO CHECK MARK) WHEN YOU ARE
NOT INTERESTED IN EXCLUDING SEPARATING ASPECTS; OTHERWISE YOU WILL
HAVE ONLY ABOUT HALF THE ASPECTS AND MAY NOT NOTICE THAT YOU ARE
MISSING HALF OF THEM.
Before we go on, make sure to turn off the Applying Only option so that we will have all the
aspects listed.

OPTIONAL ASTROLOGICAL INFORMATION
We find that when we are not certain about the time of birth, it is useful to have less data on the
screen. Therefore, for such cases, we allow you to exclude the Moon, Vertex, Ascendant, and
Midheaven. Also, you may exclude the True North Node if you like. This is done by changing
the Check Boxes on the seventh line of the Data Entry Area. As is the case with the Applying
Only function, a blank box indicates the function is not working, and a check mark tells the
program to include the function.
There are five check boxes on line 7. They control the following:
NN:
to include or exclude the True North Node
ACMC: to include or exclude the Ascendant and Midheaven
VT:
to include or exclude the Vertex
CH:
to include or exclude Chiron
Moon: to include or exclude the Moon
These options can be very useful because otherwise, you could get lost in a mountain of aspects
and data that you cannot even be certain about because you do not have the exact time and place
of birth. By eliminating these pieces of data, you can focus on the astrological data that you are
sure about.

HOUSES
Advanced versions of the MagiSoft program include a feature that lets you calculate ten
popular house systems. The basic MagiSoft V 2.36 does not include this advanced feature. It is
described here so that if you order Upgrades or advanced features for your software, you will
understand how to use it.
295

None of the Magi Society’s research could verify that any of the popular house systems
was useful and/or valid. In spite of this, we have programmed a powerful House feature into your
new MagiSoft program, just in case you want to check on what most astrologers write about.
Houses can be accessed using [(CTRL) + <M>]; when you enter this hotkey combination, the
HOUSE WINDOW will pop up. To view a chart in the format of any of the house systems listed
in the window, simply click on the little circle that corresponds to the house system you want to
use, and click the DONE button. When you do this, you will notice that the declinations of the
planets disappear since traditional astrology has no place for declinations in the houses. What is
nice and unique about MagiSoft’s house feature is that you can employ the house feature along
with transits and Combined Alignment Charts. In other words, you can see the transits of the
planets through the houses, and you can compare two charts and see which houses the connected
person’s planets are placed. You do this by using red flashing planets and mode 8 (which you get
when you enter [<alt> + <8>]. Like the function keys, the House feature in MagiSoft is designed
for use only in modes 1 and mode 8. Here is how the House feature can be used in each of these
two modes:

Houses In Mode 1
You can use the House feature in mode 1 and the five functions keys that draw aspect
lines (F5, F9, F10, F11, F12) can be used to check for aspects. F1 will clear all lines.

Houses in Mode 8
Use this mode to create a Combined House Chart. Such a chart allows you to compare
two person’s charts on the basis of the houses that each person’s natal planets make to each other.
For example, with person A and person B, you can see which of person A’s houses the other
person’s natal planets are in. For example: is person B’s Jupiter in person A’s seventh house?
Some astrologers find this useful. (We have no evidence verifying or contradicting this belief.)
In case you want to check on this yourself, simply create a CAC of two persons with flashing
planets the way we have explained, and then enter [<ctrl> + <M>] and choose a house system.
BEFORE YOU ENTER [<CTRL> + <M>], MAKE SURE THERE ARE NO ASPECT LINES
DRAWN ON THE CAC. THIS MEANS YOU MUST ENTER <F1> WHICH REMOVES ALL
ASPECT LINES; if you do not do this you will get an error message and will have to reload your
MagiSoft program.
You can also check for your transits through the houses. To do this, load your chart and
open the COMPARISON window and enter the date for which you want to check the house
transits into the Date Box of the Comparison Window. Turn on the red flashing planets and then
apply the House feature by using [<ctrl> + <M>]. You will be able to see which red flashing
planets are in which of your houses at the time of the transits. You can use the Time Increment
feature to move the transiting date forwards or backwards. This is done by entering [<ctrl> +
<left arrow> or <right arrow>]. Remember that in mode 8, when we use these keys, the date that
is incremented (changed) is the date that is in the COMPARISON box, which is the one displayed
in red on the upper right corner of the graphics portion of your screen. This date is the Transit
date. By setting up and using the MagiSoft program in this way, you can literally see the planets
moving through the houses during the transits.

WHEN THE HOUSE WINDOW IS OPEN, DO NOT CLICK YOUR MOUSE ANYWHERE

CHECKING FOR HIGH BALANCE OF PLANETS
In Chapter 17 of our third book, Magi Astrology: the Key to Success in Love and Money,
we revealed a very powerful secret of Magi Astrology. We are referring to the concepts of HIGH
BALANCE OF PLANETS and MAXIMUM BALANCE OF PLANETS. When the Magi
Society has more time, and when the stars are right, we will use these concepts to bring about a
worldwide acceptance of the validity of astrology. The F5 function key is designed to help you
detect when there is High Balance. This is a new function key available only in MagiSoft
versions 3.00 and higher. When you enter this key, you draw lines connecting all 30-degree type
aspects. To check for High Balance of Planets, please make sure the Time Increment is set to 1.0
days (this is the default setting and it is the one MagiSoft uses when you load the program). Then
go to mode 1 by entering [<ALT> + <1>] and load the chart that you wish to analyze for High
Balance. If you now use the [<CTRL> + <right arrow> or <left arrow>] to advance the chart to
the day after birth or to go back to the day before birth, you will be able to pick out the days of
High Balance. This takes some training and experience, but if you look for the Pivot Planets that
have at least two aspect lines drawn to them under the F5 filter, and use the Time Increment to
advance a day and go back a day, you will train yourself to be able to spot the days when there is
High Balance.

SYMMETRICAL PLANETARY GEOMETRY
The F5 filter is also helpful as an aid in spotting Symmetrical Planetary Geometry. The
most helpful symmetrical patterns are the ones that are created by connecting only 30-degree type
aspects, and this is exactly what the F5 filter does. With this filter, you will see symmetrical
patterns within all the lines that are drawn.

HOW TO SEND MAGI ASTROLOGY CHARTS BY EMAIL
Several members have asked us how in the world they can create a Magi Astrology Chart
that can be sent through email. They want to share the MAGIc of Magi Astrology with their
friends and clients by using email. They want to use email to send a copy of a CAC or other chart
created by MagiSoft. After all, a CAC is very impressive.
It is very easy to send a CAC or any Magi Astrology Chart by email. When you use
MagiSoft and have created a chart you want to send, you simply have to save the chart into a
document file (like a Word document) that you can then send as an attachment in your emails.
Follow the steps below in order to save the actual chart into a file that you can attach to your
email.
First you must use MagiSoft to create the chart that you want to send by email. Once you have
done this, while you are still running the MagiSoft program and it is showing the chart you want
to send by email, you should go to Full Screen Mode by entering [<Ctrl> + <G>]. Then press the
<Print Screen> key that is on your keyboard (and is a part of all Windows Keyboards). By
pressing the Print Screen key, you are instructing your computer to save whatever image is on
your computer's screen into a special place reserved in RAM or on your hard drive, and you will
be then be able to paste this image into any file. For example, you can paste the Magi Astrology
chart image you saved onto a blank page of a Word document by using the Microsoft Word
program. Here are the exact steps to paste the image of the Magi Astrology chart into a Word
document:
1. With the MagiSoft program still showing the chart in Full Screen mode, enter [<Ctrl> + <G>]
in order to go back to the Main Screen of the MagiSoft program

298

2. Then minimize the MagiSoft screen by clicking on the Minimize Button (the leftmost button
among the three buttons at the top right corner of the MagiSoft Main Screen)
3. Now load Microsoft Word and simply create a new document (by clicking the File Menu and
click on New and follow the instructions on creating a new document); once the Word
program shows you the blank page, you can paste the Magi Astrology chart onto the page if
you just enter [<Ctrl> + <V>]; the Magi Astrology Chart will be pasted onto the Word
document.
You can then make comments or add any notes you like into the Word document. When you are
finished, just save the document and attach it to your email.

TROUBLE-SHOOTING
With over 13000 copies of our MagiSoft program installed worldwide, we now have had a lot of
experience with our programs. Here are the most common problems that our members have
encountered while installing MagiSoft.
Below are common installation problems and simple solutions:
1. The MagiSoft program can be installed only on the main hard drive (the boot drive) of your
computer and it must be the C: drive. The C: drive is the main drive in 99.5% of all computer
systems and that is the standard configuration in the computer industry. If your computer system
is different, you should correct this and have your operating system installed on the C: drive
because you will have problems with other computer software as well as MagiSoft.
2. While installing MagiSoft, about 1 percent of our members run into an error message referring
to the name of some file when installing MagiSoft. If you get such a message, it is almost always
due to the fact that a file that is a normal part of the Windows operating system is missing from
your computer system, or the file is corrupted. You need to correct this problem. One way is to
run Scandisk. Another way is to reload all of your operating system's standard files. (One way
this problem could have occurred on your computer is if you UNinstalled a program. When you
uninstall a program, the act of uninstalling can remove a "shared file" that you actually need for
other programs. This can easily occur if you click the wrong buttons during the uninstall
procedure.)
SOME PRINTERS HAVE TO BE RESET USING PRINT SETUP
Finally, there is just one other known peculiarity about your MagiSoft program. If you have
trouble using MagiSoft to print any charts or anything else it is supposed to print, the problem has
always been due to a mismatched setting between your printer and the MagiSoft program. To
correct this, you need to load MagiSoft and click on the File Menu, then click on Print Setup.
You have to check the settings of your printer and make sure the settings are correct. For
example, you want the printer to be set to print 8.5 by 11 inch paper. With some printers, you
may actually have to reset these settings each time you close and reload MagiSoft.
YOU DO NOT HAVE THE HELIOCENTRIC UPGRADE

299

The Magi Society offers a Heliocentric Upgrade for its software; when the upgrade is loaded, the
MagiSoft program becomes version 6.22 or higher. You did not yet order the Heliocentric
Upgrade and you should make a note of this:
When the Heliocentric Upgrade is installed, the hotkey combination of [<Ctrl> + <H>] is a
helio/geo toggle switch. If you are in geocentric mode, pressing [<Ctrl> + <H>] will tell the
MagiSoft program to switch the graphics from Geocentric to Heliocentric, and vice versa. Since
your program does not have the Heliocentric Upgrade, when you enter [<Ctrl> + <H>], the Magi
Astrology Chart will have no planets shown because your program has no heliocentric ability. In
other words, you would get a blank chart. This is not a bug; it is the way the program was
designed. To get back to a geocentric chart that shows the positions of the planets in geocentric
longitudes and declinations, you have to enter [<Ctrl> + <H>] a second time. You get the same
results if you choose the Commands Menu and click on Heliocentric/Geo since this does the same
thing as if you enter [<Ctrl> + <H>].
A HINT FOR MAGISOFT USERS
This tip might be helpful to you. If you run into trouble trying to do something, and things do not
seem to be working out, simply restart the program. First turn off your program by clicking the
white arrow on the button with the “X” at the upper right corner of the program’s Main Screen.
You will get a window asking you if you want to save changes in the default: ALWAYS CLICK
THE “NO” BUTTON. Then double-click on the MagiSoft Icon to reload MagiSoft and try again.

bug or two. But do not worry; the program works fabulously well and we are not aware of any
bugs.

WAR AGAINST TERRORISM
November 5, 2001
These weeks since September 11 have been very trying, and they have tormented our
souls. Almost all of us are incessantly worried about matters like:
What is going to happen to the US and the world in the months and years just ahead?
Will there be massive terrorist attacks on us using biological weapons? Or even nuclear
weapons?
Will we enter into an endless war with the militant Islamic extremists?
What's
going
to
happen
to
the
US
economy
and
our
jobs?
What kind of world will our children have to live in decades from now?
300

Such uncertainties are wrenching at our guts and pounding our psyche. But at the Magi
Society, we see great hope in the stars, and we never lose our faith in God Providence.
At this crucial time in history, we think it is a good idea to take some deep breathes and
recall the miracles that have occurred like what happened the last time the world was on
the edge of what seemed like certain holocaust.
Let us look back and learn from what happened just 12 years ago and recall the ending
of the Cold War.

THE ENDING OF THE COLD WAR WAS A MIRACLE
From the late 1950's until mid-1989, the whole world was under the fear of what seemed
like an inevitable nuclear conflict that would wipe out all life on Earth. The differences
between the two countries seemed absolutely irreconcilable. The USSR and the USA
had tens of thousands of nuclear warheads aimed at each other. From within the Soviet
Union, the Russians had thousands of nuclear warheads on missiles aimed at our cities.
Each warhead could destroy even our largest city. Even scarier was the fact the Soviets
had hundreds of submarines just off our shores with thousands of nuclear warheads on
top of missiles that could strike us within ten minutes of launch. We ourselves had
surrounded the USSR with thousands of nuclear warheads of our own atop of thousands
of missiles aimed at them. Mutually Assured Destruction was the strategy of both
countries. Both countries had a hair-trigger mentality and a nuclear war could erupt

NOSTRADAMUS
Oct 15, 2001
One of the outcomes of the September 11 tragedies has been a renewed interest in
Nostradamus and his writings. Below is our opinion of Nostradamus:
Since the key to Nostradamus are the "prophecies" that he wrote, any analysis of
Nostradamus first requires a discussion about Free Will.
Ever since humankind could think, we have wondered about the future and whether or
not we have Free Will. We have been wondering about this for thousands of years and
the world's best minds have spent countless lifetimes grappling with this issue. In spite
of these monumental efforts, even now, no one has actually arrived at a completely
intellectually satisfying answer to the question of Free Will.
At this time, the common wisdom is that each of us was born with Free Will. But this is
seemingly contradicted by the fact Astrology Really Works. Astrology and Free Will
seem to be contradictory.
But they are not.
At the Magi Society, we believe in both astrology and Free Will. As we explain in the
"Predicting the Future " section of this website, all of the major trends in our lives are
predictable by the stars. But we have Free Will and the decisions we ourselves make will
determine both the extent and the details of each major trend in our lives.
What this means is that we can use astrology to predict the direction and duration of a
major trend in our lives but the details and magnitude of any trend is within our own
control and subject to our God given Free will.
Now that we have discussed Free Will, we can talk about Nostradamus a little more
clearly.
Nostradamus wrote a book in 1555, and many devotees claim he made precise
prophecies that have come true.
We are very skeptical of Nostradamus because of what he did NOT predict as opposed
to what he did predict. For example, Nostradamus did not foresee things like:
Airplanes and men landing on the Moon
Electricity and modern electrical appliances such as lights and refrigerators
Television and mass communications equipment like telephones and cell phones
Vaccines, antibiotics, heart transplants and other marvels of modern medicine
Democracy and the right of citizens to vote
Instead of making accurate predictions like any of those listed above, all of the writings
of Nostradamus predicted war, catastrophes, and other horrors. Frankly, this is not

303

difficult to do. All of you could have written about calamities, war and disasters and
sooner or later, some of them would come true. But what about the GOOD stuff?
Since Nostradamus could not foresee men landing on the Moon, electricity and lights,
democracy and the right to vote, what use were his predictions?
They serve no use.
During the time of Nostradamus, the kingdoms in Europe were constantly at war so for
him to predict war would occur is as useful as saying the Sun will rise in the morning.
Even his prognostications of disaster are so vague as to render them worthless. For
example, he talks about a "ball of fire" and the destruction of the "city of mountains." But
many cities were built around, or on top of, mountains so the phrase "city of mountains"
is so vague it could mean any of hundreds of cities. And a "ball of fire" could mean
earthquakes or just a huge fire. It does not take a prophet to know there will always be
fires and earthquakes.
We believe Nostradamus was purposely vague because he had no predictive ability and
he knew it.
Nostradamus wrote often that the "Eagle" would be waging war. But the Eagle was the
symbol of many kingdoms and empires during his time and before, including the
Roman Empire. In fact, the Eagle is the most commonly chosen symbol for a kingdom.
Therefore, any prediction involving an "Eagle" was worthless.
Some enthusiasts of Nostradamus say that September 11 is the beginning of a 23-year
worldwide war that will be the most devastating war ever. DO NOT BELIEVE IT.
This is instead a time when we can rid ourselves of a threat to civilization and we will
succeed in doing so.
Fortunately, Bin Laden jumped the gun and acted too soon and will now be unable to
achieve his maniacal ambitions. Tim Russert (of NBC's Meet the Press) explained on
September 8 that Bin Laden's goals have been to take control of Pakistan because it has
The Bomb, then take over Saudi Arabia, and then the rest of the Islamic countries, and
finally to wage a war directly against the US. But Bin Laden made a crucial
miscalculation and thought the US would not send troops into Afghanistan to eliminate
him. Bin Laden thought the US would not have the stomach or courage to actually go
get him. But the US has resolved to get him, and all his lieutenants. And both God
Providence and the stars are on the side of the US led coalition against global terrorism.
A few are asking: Is there a "peaceful" solution possible, and can we negotiate?
Not really. You can make peace with anyone who is not determined to kill you. But Bin
Laden has proven he likes to kill and would be willing to kill anyone that does not agree
with him. The assassination of Anwar Sadat is proof that you cannot make peace with
Bin Laden. Sadat made peace with Israel and was killed because of it. Ayman AlZawahiri is the maniac who masterminded the Sadat assassination; they killed Sadat for
making peace. Ayman Al-Zawahiri's Egyptian terrorist group merged with Bin Laden's
own terrorist organization to form Al Qaeda and now Ayman Al-Zawahiri is Bin

Laden's second in command. Anyone who hopes for negotiations should learn from
